$$\forall i \in [Q], \ \underline{\mathsf{hct}}_{f_i} + \Delta \left[ \frac{\mathbf{c}_{\mathbf{s},i}^\mathsf{T} \mathbf{G}^{-1}(\mathbf{A}) - \mathbf{c}_i^\mathsf{T}}{\Delta} \right] + \mathbf{c}_i^\mathsf{T} + \mathsf{dct}_{f_i} = \tilde{\mathbf{s}}_i^\mathsf{T} \mathbf{A} + \tilde{\mathbf{e}}_i^\mathsf{T}$$
where  $\tilde{\mathbf{s}}_i^\mathsf{T} = \mathbf{u}_{f_i}^\mathsf{T} + \mathbf{s}_i^\mathsf{T}, \ \tilde{\mathbf{e}}_i^\mathsf{T} = \mathbf{e}_i^\mathsf{T} + \mathbf{e}_B^\mathsf{T} \mathbf{R}_{f_i} + \mathbf{e}_{f_i}^\mathsf{T}$ 
(8)

Figure 7: Version II: Special Homomorphic Evaluation Procedure for Computing GSW ciphertexts of  $\mathbf{s}_i^{\mathsf{T}} \mathbf{A} + \mathbf{e}_i^{\mathsf{T}}$ . Each  $\mathbf{c}_{\mathbf{s},i}$  has dimension  $n \log q$  and bit length  $n \log q \log q$ , which is sublinear in  $L = \ell \log q$  if  $n \log q \ll \ell$ .

depends on the top part of the ciphertext  $hct_{f_i}$ . Different from Version I,  $hct_{f_i}$  is now the result of evaluating  $f_i(\mathbf{r})$  and hence is only correlated with  $hct(\mathbf{r})$  and  $f_i$  which depends on matrices  $\mathbf{D}$ ,  $\mathbf{A}$ , and hence independent of  $\mathbf{s}_i$ .

Comparison In prior constructions [DQV<sup>+</sup>21, WW21], the LWE secrets  $\tilde{s}$  produced in the scheme are far from random. In particular, this was leveraged by [JLLS23] to launch a polynomial-time attack on [DQV<sup>+</sup>21].

<u>Drawbacks</u> Now that  $(\tilde{\mathbf{s}}_i, \tilde{\mathbf{e}}_i)$  is jointly random, can we reduce the security of Version II to some LWE-with-hints assumption with random hints? We show below that this could be done, however, the resulting assumption needs to postulate security of LWE-based encodings with an "unnatural" distribution, in particular, they are provably not pseudorandom given the hints.

We observe that there is a reduction  $\mathcal{R}_2$  that given a sample from the following "smaller" distribution can emulate the distribution of Version II:

$$\text{Real}_{v2}: (\text{hpk, hct}(\mathbf{r}), \{\mathbf{D}_i, \widehat{\mathbf{c}}_i\}_i, \mathbf{A}, \text{dct}), \text{ where } \widehat{\mathbf{c}}_i^{\mathsf{T}} = \mathbf{r}^{\mathsf{T}} \mathbf{D}_i - \mathbf{u}_{f_i}^{\mathsf{T}} \mathbf{G} + \widehat{\mathbf{e}}_i^{\mathsf{T}}$$

Above, components hpk, hct( $\mathbf{r}$ ),  $\mathbf{D}$ ,  $\mathbf{A}$ , dct are sampled exactly as in Version II. Therefore, the reduction  $\mathcal{R}_2$  just needs to emulate the missing components ( $\tilde{\mathbf{s}}_i$ ,  $\tilde{\mathbf{e}}_i$ ,  $\mathbf{c}_i$ ,  $\mathbf{c}_{s,i}$ ) in Version II. Leveraging that ( $\tilde{\mathbf{s}}_i$ ,  $\tilde{\mathbf{e}}_i$ ) are random,  $\mathcal{R}_2$  can sample them internally, which implicitly defines  $\mathbf{s}_i^{\mathsf{T}} = \tilde{\mathbf{s}}_i^{\mathsf{T}} - \mathbf{u}_{f_i}^{\mathsf{T}}$  and  $\mathbf{e}_i^{\mathsf{T}} = \tilde{\mathbf{e}}_i^{\mathsf{T}} - (\mathbf{e}_{f_i}^{\mathsf{T}} + \mathbf{e}_{\mathbf{B}}^{\mathsf{T}} \mathbf{R}_{f_i})$ . Next, the correctness constraint (Equation (8)) gives a way to emulate  $\mathbf{c}_i$  as follows:

<span id="page-37-2"></span>
$$\mathbf{c}_i \text{ emulation:} \quad \mathbf{c}_i^{\mathsf{T}} = (\tilde{\mathbf{s}}_i^{\mathsf{T}} \mathbf{A} + \tilde{\mathbf{e}}_i^{\mathsf{T}}) - \underline{\mathsf{hct}}_{f_i} - \mathsf{dct}_{f_i} \pmod{\Delta}$$
 (9)

{38}------------------------------------------------

Finally,  $\mathbf{c}_{\mathbf{s},i}$ , which should encrypt  $\mathbf{s}_{i}^{\mathsf{T}}\mathbf{G} = \tilde{\mathbf{s}}_{i}^{\mathsf{T}}\mathbf{G} - \mathbf{u}_{f_{i}}^{\mathsf{T}}\mathbf{G}$  can be emulated using  $\hat{\mathbf{c}}_{i}$ :

<span id="page-38-1"></span>
$$\mathbf{c}_{\mathbf{s},i}$$
 emulation:  $\mathbf{c}_{\mathbf{s},i}^{\mathsf{T}} = \widehat{\mathbf{c}}_{i}^{\mathsf{T}} + \widetilde{\mathbf{s}}_{i}^{\mathsf{T}}\mathbf{G}$  (10)

Hence, any property of the distribution in Version II translates to some property of  $Real_{v2}$ , and vice versa.

Examining the distribution  $\text{Real}_{v2}$ , it contains circular LWE encodings –  $\text{hct}(\mathbf{r})$  circularly encrypts  $\mathbf{r}$  under  $\mathbf{r}$ , dct encrypts  $\mathbf{I}_{\ell} \otimes \mathbf{G}^{\mathsf{T}} \cdot \mathbf{r}$  under  $\mathbf{U}$ , and  $\widehat{\mathbf{c}}_{i}$  encrypts  $\mathbf{u}_{f_{i}}$  under  $\mathbf{r}$ . It appears that by the commonly used circular LWE security rationale, one could postulate the pseudorandomness of  $\text{Real}_{v2}$ , which would imply some form of the security of Version II.

However, this is false. Real<sub>v2</sub> is provably not pseudorandom, because the correctness condition (Equation (8)) of Version II translates (via  $\mathcal{R}_2$ ) into an efficiently verifiable constraint on Real<sub>v2</sub> that truly random encodings do not satisfy.

To unravel the apparent contradiction, it is instrumental to note that the encoding  $\hat{\mathbf{c}}$  is not a "safe" circular encoding. In general, a circular encoding  $\mathbf{t}^{\mathsf{T}}\mathbf{H} + f(\mathbf{t}) + \mathbf{e}^{\mathsf{T}}$  is only secure if the encrypted message  $f(\mathbf{t})$  is independent of the encoding randomness  $(\mathbf{H}, \mathbf{e})$  (a trivial counterexamples is  $f(\mathbf{t}) = -\mathbf{t}^{\mathsf{T}} \cdot \mathbf{H}$ ). However,  $\hat{\mathbf{c}}$  violates this rule-of-thumb: The message  $\mathbf{u}_{f_i}$  depends on the random matrix  $\mathbf{D}_i$  used to encode it. The correlation exists because  $\mathbf{u}_{f_i}$  depends on the function  $f_i$ , which computes  $f_i(\mathbf{r}) = -\Delta [\mathbf{r}^{\mathsf{T}}\mathbf{D}_i\mathbf{G}^{-1}(\mathbf{A})/\Delta]$  and is dependent on  $\mathbf{D}_i$ .

We distill a take-away message from the above discussion. For any assumption that contains LWE-based encodings, we view the lack of plausible pseudorandomness of the encodings problematic, as it stands at odds with our intuition that security based on LWE encodings relies on their pseudorandomness<sup>8</sup>.

Therefore, our goal is to formulate an LWE-with-hint assumption, where the LWE encodings in the real distribution are switched to random in the ideal distribution. Towards this, in Version III we will introduce a URS (uniform random CRS), and show simulation security, namely, the encodings and URS can be simulated using  $\tilde{\mathbf{s}}_{i}^{\mathsf{T}}\mathbf{A} + \tilde{\mathbf{e}}_{i}^{\mathsf{T}}$ .

Comparison In all prior oblivious LWE sampler and xiO constructions [BDGM20, DQV<sup>+</sup>21, WW21, GP21, BDGM22], the underlying hardness / assumption postulates indistinguishability security, and lack natural pseudorandomness variants of their assumptions.

Version III: GSW Rerandomization, Pseudorandom LWE-with-Hint, and Simulation Security Towards the aforementioned goal of relying on pseudorandom LWE-with-hint assumption and achieving simulation security, Version III uses a technique introduced in [GP21] that re-randomizes the GSW ciphertext before dual-GSW homomorphic decryption, as described in Figure 8. The re-randomization uses sufficiently wide random Gaussian matrices  $\mathbf{R}^* = \{\mathbf{R}_i^*\}_{i \in [Q]}$  contained in the URS. In particular, after Step 1) obtaining the GSW ciphertext hct $f_i$ , Step 2) "rerandomizes" the ciphertext to

$$\mathsf{hct'} = \mathsf{hct}_{f_i} + \overline{\mathbf{B}} \mathbf{R}_i^* = \begin{pmatrix} \mathbf{B} \widetilde{\mathbf{R}}_i \\ (\mathbf{r}^\mathsf{T} \mathbf{B} + \mathbf{e}_{\mathbf{B}}^\mathsf{T}) \widetilde{\mathbf{R}}_i + f_i(\mathbf{r}) \end{pmatrix}, \text{ where } \widetilde{\mathbf{R}}_i = (\mathbf{R}_{f_i} + \mathbf{R}_i^*)$$

Following that, evaluation proceeds identically as in Version II.

Advantage We first formulate a distribution Realv3 from which Version III can be emulated, and

<span id="page-38-0"></span><sup>&</sup>lt;sup>8</sup>This should be separated from LWE-based constructions, e.g., NIZK, where pseudorandomness does not hold but ZK or indistinguishability holds. Such behaviors are the result of careful design, whereas when formulating assumptions, we are considering LWE encodings that we do not fully know how to analyze.

show that the LWE encodings in Real<sub>v3</sub> now follow sound circular security rationale.

$$\begin{aligned} & \text{Real}_{\text{v3}} : \text{encodings} = \left( \text{hpk} = \overline{\mathbf{B}}, \, \text{hct}(\mathbf{r}), \, \{ \text{hct}_{0,i} = \overline{\mathbf{B}} \widetilde{\mathbf{R}}_i \}, \, \mathbf{D}, \, \{ \widehat{\mathbf{c}}_i \}, \, \mathbf{A}, \, \text{dct} \right), \, \text{hint} = \{ \mathbf{R}_i^* \} \\ & \text{where } \widetilde{\mathbf{R}}_i = \mathbf{R}_{f_i} + \mathbf{R}_i^*, \, \widehat{\mathbf{c}}_i = \mathbf{r}^\mathsf{T} \mathbf{D}_i + \widehat{\mathbf{e}}_i^\mathsf{T} - \mathbf{u}_i^\mathsf{T} \mathbf{G}, \, \mathbf{u}_i^\mathsf{T} \mathbf{G} = \text{vec}(\mathbf{G}^{-1}(-\mathbf{B}\widetilde{\mathbf{R}}))^\mathsf{T} \mathbf{U}^\mathsf{T} \mathbf{G} = f^{\text{circ}}(\mathbf{U}, \, \text{hct}_0) \; . \end{aligned}$$

Additionally, (hpk, hct( $\mathbf{r}$ ),  $\mathbf{D}$ ,  $\mathbf{A}$ , dct,  $\mathbf{R}^*$ ) are sampled, and  $\mathbf{R}_{f_i}$ ,  $\mathbf{u}_i$  computed just as in Version III. To emulate the full distribution of Version III, a reduction  $\mathcal{R}_3$  given a sample from Real<sub>v3</sub> needs to emulate the missing terms ( $\tilde{\mathbf{s}}_i$ ,  $\tilde{\mathbf{e}}_i$ ,  $\mathbf{c}_i$ ,  $\mathbf{c}_{s,i}$ ) similarly to  $\mathcal{R}_2$ . Because the distribution of  $\tilde{\mathbf{s}}_i$ ,  $\tilde{\mathbf{e}}_i$  are random and independent of all the components in Real<sub>v3</sub>, they can be sampled by  $\mathcal{R}_3$  internally,  $\mathbf{c}_{s,i}$  is emulated by  $\hat{\mathbf{c}}_i + \tilde{\mathbf{s}}_i^\mathsf{T} \mathbf{G}$  as in Equation (9), and  $\mathbf{c}_i$  is emulated according to the new correctness condition (Equation (11)):

<span id="page-39-2"></span>New 
$$\mathbf{c}_i$$
 emulation:  $\mathbf{c}_i = (\tilde{\mathbf{s}}_i^\mathsf{T} \mathbf{A} + \tilde{\mathbf{e}}_i^\mathsf{T}) - \underline{\mathsf{hct}}_{0,i} - \mathsf{dct}_i \pmod{\Delta}$  (12)

Thanks to re-randomization, the LWE encodings encodings in Real<sub>v3</sub> are now safe circular encoding.  $hct(\mathbf{r})$ ,  $hct_{0,i}$ , dct are standard circular encodings. We further observe that  $\hat{\mathbf{c}}_i$  now encrypts a message  $\mathbf{u}_i$  using *independent* randomness  $(\mathbf{D}, \hat{\mathbf{e}})$ . This is because  $\mathbf{u}_i$  depends on  $\mathbf{U}$  and  $\mathbf{B}\tilde{\mathbf{R}}_i$ . Thanks to smudging,  $\tilde{\mathbf{R}}_i = \mathbf{R}_{f_i} + \mathbf{R}_i^*$  is a random Gaussian matrix and hence  $\mathbf{u}_i$  is independent of  $\mathbf{D}$  and  $\hat{\mathbf{e}}$ . Therefore, by circular security rationale, the encodings alone is pseudorandom. This overcomes the drawback of Version II.

{40}------------------------------------------------

Our Pseudorandom LWE-with-hints Assumption: We explore whether the LWE encodings encodings is still pseudorandom, at the presence of hint, by formulating an LWE-with-hints assumption. While encodings alone is pseudorandom by circular security, and  $\mathbf{R}_i^*$ 's are marginally random, their joint distribution is subject to a constraint implied by the correctness condition of Version III. Hence, the main question is when encodings is switched to random in an ideal distribution, how should the distribution of  $\mathbf{R}_i^*$  change accordingly to ensure that the constraint is still satisfied?

Let's examine the distribution of  $\mathbf{R}_{i}^{*}$ . In the real distribution Real<sub>v3</sub>, it is a random Gaussian matrix subject to the following constraint:

$$\mathbf{R}_{i}^{*} \leftarrow \mathcal{D}_{\sigma_{0}}^{m \times \ell}$$
, conditioned on  $\operatorname{hct}_{f_{i}} + \overline{\mathbf{B}} \mathbf{R}_{i}^{*} = \operatorname{hct}_{0,i} + \begin{pmatrix} \mathbf{0} \\ f_{i}(\mathbf{r}) \end{pmatrix}$ 

Furthermore, the correctness equality of Version III is equivalent to an equality showing that  $f_i(\mathbf{r})$  can be computed publicly from existing LWE encodings (hct<sub>0,i</sub>,  $\hat{\mathbf{c}}_i$ , dct) with overwhelming probability.

<span id="page-40-0"></span>**Claim 1.** The correctness constraint in Version III is equivalent to the following equality:

$$f_{i}(\mathbf{r}) \stackrel{w.h.p}{=} \widetilde{f_{i}}(\mathsf{hct}_{0,i}, \widehat{\mathbf{c}}_{i}, \mathsf{dct}) = \left[ \frac{-\widehat{\mathbf{c}}_{i}^{\mathsf{T}} \mathbf{G}^{-1}(\mathbf{A}) + \mathsf{dct}_{i} - \underline{\mathsf{hct}}_{0,i}}{\Delta} \right] \cdot \Delta, \ \mathsf{dct}_{i} = \mathsf{vec}(\mathbf{G}^{-1}(-\overline{\mathsf{hct}}_{0,i}))^{\mathsf{T}} \cdot \mathsf{dct}$$

*Proof.* The proof follows from algebraic derivation, starting from the correctness of Version III.

$$\begin{split} \tilde{\mathbf{s}}_{i}^{\mathsf{T}}\mathbf{A} + \tilde{\mathbf{e}}_{i}^{\mathsf{T}} &= \underline{\mathsf{hct}}_{0,i} + f_{i}(\mathbf{r}) + \Delta \left[ \frac{\mathbf{c}_{s_{i},i}^{\mathsf{T}}\mathbf{G}^{-1}(\mathbf{A}) - \mathbf{c}_{i}^{\mathsf{T}}}{\Delta} \right] + \mathbf{c}_{i}^{\mathsf{T}} + \mathsf{dct}_{i} \\ f_{i}(\mathbf{r}) &= \tilde{\mathbf{s}}_{i}^{\mathsf{T}}\mathbf{A} + \tilde{\mathbf{e}}_{i}^{\mathsf{T}} - \underline{\mathsf{hct}}_{0,i} - \mathsf{dct}_{i} - \mathbf{c}_{i}^{\mathsf{T}} - \Delta \left[ \frac{\mathbf{c}_{s_{i},i}^{\mathsf{T}}\mathbf{G}^{-1}(\mathbf{A}) - \mathbf{c}_{i}^{\mathsf{T}}}{\Delta} \right] \\ &= \tilde{\mathbf{s}}_{i}^{\mathsf{T}}\mathbf{A} + \tilde{\mathbf{e}}_{i}^{\mathsf{T}} - \underline{\mathsf{hct}}_{0,i} - \mathsf{dct}_{i} - \mathbf{c}_{i}^{\mathsf{T}} - \left( \mathbf{c}_{s_{i},i}^{\mathsf{T}}\mathbf{G}^{-1}(\mathbf{A}) - \mathbf{c}_{i}^{\mathsf{T}} \right) + \left( \left( \mathbf{c}_{s_{i},i}^{\mathsf{T}}\mathbf{G}^{-1}(\mathbf{A}) - \mathbf{c}_{i}^{\mathsf{T}} \right) \bmod \Delta \right) \\ &= \tilde{\mathbf{s}}_{i}^{\mathsf{T}}\mathbf{A} + \tilde{\mathbf{e}}_{i}^{\mathsf{T}} - \underline{\mathsf{hct}}_{0,i} - \mathsf{dct}_{i} - \mathbf{c}_{i}^{\mathsf{T}} - \left( \tilde{\mathbf{c}}_{i}^{\mathsf{T}}\mathbf{G}^{-1}(\mathbf{A}) + \tilde{\mathbf{s}}_{i}^{\mathsf{T}}\mathbf{A} - \mathbf{c}_{i}^{\mathsf{T}} \right) + \left( \left( \tilde{\mathbf{c}}_{i}^{\mathsf{T}}\mathbf{G}^{-1}(\mathbf{A}) + \tilde{\mathbf{s}}_{i}^{\mathsf{T}}\mathbf{A} - \mathbf{c}_{i}^{\mathsf{T}} \right) + \left( \left( \tilde{\mathbf{c}}_{i}^{\mathsf{T}}\mathbf{G}^{-1}(\mathbf{A}) + \tilde{\mathbf{s}}_{i}^{\mathsf{T}}\mathbf{A} - \mathbf{c}_{i}^{\mathsf{T}} \right) + \left( \tilde{\mathbf{c}}_{i}^{\mathsf{T}}\mathbf{A} - \tilde{\mathbf{c}}_{i}^{\mathsf{T}} \right) + \left( \tilde{\mathbf{c}}_{i}^{\mathsf{T}}\mathbf{G}^{-1}(\mathbf{A}) + \tilde{\mathbf{s}}_{i}^{\mathsf{T}}\mathbf{A} - \mathbf{c}_{i}^{\mathsf{T}} \right) + \left( \tilde{\mathbf{c}}_{i}^{\mathsf{T}}\mathbf{G}^{-1}(\mathbf{A}) + \tilde{\mathbf{s}}_{i}^{\mathsf{T}}\mathbf{A} - \mathbf{c}_{i}^{\mathsf{T}} \right) + \left( \tilde{\mathbf{c}}_{i}^{\mathsf{T}}\mathbf{G}^{-1}(\mathbf{A}) + \tilde{\mathbf{s}}_{i}^{\mathsf{T}}\mathbf{A} - \mathbf{c}_{i}^{\mathsf{T}} \right) + \left( \tilde{\mathbf{c}}_{i}^{\mathsf{T}}\mathbf{G}^{-1}(\mathbf{A}) + \tilde{\mathbf{s}}_{i}^{\mathsf{T}}\mathbf{A} - \mathbf{c}_{i}^{\mathsf{T}} \right) + \left( \tilde{\mathbf{c}}_{i}^{\mathsf{T}}\mathbf{G}^{-1}(\mathbf{A}) + \tilde{\mathbf{s}}_{i}^{\mathsf{T}}\mathbf{A} - \mathbf{c}_{i}^{\mathsf{T}} \right) + \left( \tilde{\mathbf{c}}_{i}^{\mathsf{T}}\mathbf{G}^{-1}(\mathbf{A}) + \tilde{\mathbf{s}}_{i}^{\mathsf{T}}\mathbf{A} - \mathbf{c}_{i}^{\mathsf{T}} \right) + \left( \tilde{\mathbf{c}}_{i}^{\mathsf{T}}\mathbf{G}^{-1}(\mathbf{A}) + \tilde{\mathbf{c}}_{i}^{\mathsf{T}}\mathbf{A} - \mathbf{c}_{i}^{\mathsf{T}} \right) + \left( \tilde{\mathbf{c}}_{i}^{\mathsf{T}}\mathbf{G}^{-1}(\mathbf{A}) + \tilde{\mathbf{c}}_{i}^{\mathsf{T}}\mathbf{A} - \mathbf{c}_{i}^{\mathsf{T}} \right) + \left( \tilde{\mathbf{c}}_{i}^{\mathsf{T}}\mathbf{G}^{-1}(\mathbf{A}) + \tilde{\mathbf{c}}_{i}^{\mathsf{T}}\mathbf{A} - \tilde{\mathbf{c}}_{i}^{\mathsf{T}} \right) + \left( \tilde{\mathbf{c}}_{i}^{\mathsf{T}}\mathbf{A} - \tilde{\mathbf{c}}_{i}^{\mathsf{T}} \right) + \left( \tilde{\mathbf{c}}_{i}^{\mathsf{T}}\mathbf{A} - \tilde{\mathbf{c}}_{i}^{\mathsf{T}} \right) + \tilde{\mathbf{c}}_{i}^{\mathsf{T}}\mathbf{A} \right) + \tilde{\mathbf{c}}_{i}^{\mathsf{T}}\mathbf{A} + \tilde{\mathbf{c}}_{i}^{\mathsf{T}}\mathbf{A} - \tilde{\mathbf{c}}_{i}^{\mathsf{T}}\mathbf{A} \right) + \tilde{\mathbf{c}}_{i}^{\mathsf{T}}\mathbf{A} + \tilde{\mathbf{c}}_{i}^{\mathsf{T}}\mathbf{A} + \tilde{\mathbf{c}}$$

The fourth equality follows from emulation of  $\mathbf{c}_{\mathbf{s}_i,i}$  by (10). The fifth equality follows from emulation of  $\mathbf{c}_i$  by (12). The last equality follows with high probability since the noise  $\tilde{\mathbf{e}}_i$  is small.

We can now formulate our pseudorandom LWE-with-hints assumption:

encodings = 
$$\{ \text{hpk} = \overline{\mathbf{B}}, \text{hct}(\mathbf{r}), \{ \text{hct}_{0,i} = \overline{\mathbf{B}} \overline{\mathbf{R}}_i \}, \mathbf{D}, \{ \widehat{\mathbf{c}}_i \}, \mathbf{A}, \text{dct} \}, \text{hint} = \{ \mathbf{R}_i^* \}$$

\mathbf{S}, \{ \mathbf{S}, \{ \mathbf{S$$

{41}------------------------------------------------

Note that the constraint on  $\mathbf{R}^*$  is efficiently verifiable. In the real distribution, the encodings contains honestly generated LWE encodings, and  $\mathbf{R}^*$  follows the Gaussian distribution subject to the constraint, while in the ideal distribution, encodings is truly random and  $\mathbf{R}^*$  is still Gaussian subject to the constraint. Furthermore, the marginal distribution of  $\mathbf{R}_i^*$  is truly random Gaussian in the real distribution (Theorem 1), and is pseudorandom Gaussian in the ideal distribution (Theorem 2). Our assumption postulates that these two distributions are indistinguishable. We show that it resists existing attacks and cryptanalytic techniques in Section 2.3.2.

Simulation Security: Our assumption immediately enables proving simulation security. Given  $\tilde{\mathbf{s}}_{i}^{\mathsf{T}}\mathbf{A} + \tilde{\mathbf{e}}_{i}^{\mathsf{T}}$ , a simulator simulates the LWE encodings and the CRS in Version III as follows: It samples encodings at random and  $\mathbf{R}_{i}^{*}$  as in the ideal distribution. Note that sampling  $\mathbf{R}_{i}^{*}$  as Gaussian with width  $\sigma_{0}$  conditioned on  $\overline{\mathbf{B}}\mathbf{R}_{i}^{*}$  being equal to a target matrix can be done efficiently if  $\overline{\mathbf{B}}$  in encodings is sampled together with a trapdoor. Then the simulator invokes  $\mathcal{R}_{3}$  to simulate the rest components in Version III. We note that the output LWE samples  $\tilde{\mathbf{s}}_{i}^{\mathsf{T}}\mathbf{A} + \tilde{\mathbf{e}}_{i}^{\mathsf{T}}$  are "programmed" in  $\mathbf{R}_{i}^{*}$  in the CRS (note this is the alternative simulation strategy of GSW).

**Construction of Functional Encoding:** Once we have an oblivious LWE sampler, it becomes easy to construct a functional encoding. The high-level idea is that the CRS of the functional encoding is exactly the CRS of the oblivious LWE sampler, namely  $\mathbf{R}^*$ . The functional encoding of an input  $\mathbf{x}$  includes all the encodings in the oblivious LWE sampler, and additionally a dual-GSW ciphertext of the binary input  $\mathbf{x}$ .

$$\mathsf{dct}(\mathbf{x}) = \mathbf{W}^\mathsf{T} \mathbf{A} + \mathbf{E}_{\mathbf{x}} + \mathbf{x} \otimes \mathbf{G}_{\ell}^\mathsf{T} \overset{\mathsf{dGSW.Eval}}{\Longrightarrow} \mathsf{dct}_{g_i} = \mathbf{w}_{g_i}^\mathsf{T} \mathbf{A} + \mathbf{e}_{g_i}^\mathsf{T} + g_i(\mathbf{x})^\mathsf{T}, \text{ for } g_i(\mathbf{x}) \in \mathbb{Z}_q^\ell$$

Using the homomorphic evaluation of dual-GSW, we can obtain a ciphertext of the output  $g_i(\mathbf{x}) \in \mathbb{Z}_q^\ell$ . To reveal the output, instead of opening  $\mathbf{w}_{g_i}$  which compromises security, we re-randomize  $\det_{g_i}$  using the obliviously sampled LWE samples and open  $\mathbf{w}_{g_i} + \tilde{\mathbf{s}}_i$ , which reveals  $g_i(\mathbf{x}) + \mathbf{e}_{g_i} + \tilde{\mathbf{e}}_i$  and hence the high order bits of  $g_i(\mathbf{x})$ . Thanks to the fact that  $\tilde{\mathbf{s}}_i$ ,  $\tilde{\mathbf{e}}_i$  are pseudorandom,  $\mathbf{w}_{g_i}$  and  $\mathbf{e}_{g_i}$  are now hidden. By a similar simulation strategy as above, we can show simulation security of the functional encoding.

# <span id="page-41-0"></span>5 Constructing Functional Encoding from CRO

<span id="page-41-1"></span>We now present the formal construction and proof of functional encoding from the CRO assumption.

**Construction 1.** In the construction, we always use the discrete Gaussian distribution with bounded norm. In particular, we use the notation  $\overline{\mathcal{D}}_{\sigma}$  to denote the conditional distribution  $x \leftarrow \mathcal{D}_{\sigma}|_{|x| \leq \sigma \sqrt{\lambda}}$ .

• Gen(1<sup> $\lambda$ </sup>, 1<sup>Q</sup>, 1<sup>K</sup>, 1<sup>L</sup>, 1<sup>d</sup>): The algorithm picks appropriate parameters  $pp = (n, m, \Delta, \kappa, p, q, \ell, \sigma, \sigma_0, \sigma_e)$  samples GSW rerandomization matrix

$$\mathbf{R}^* = (\mathbf{R}_1^*, \dots, \mathbf{R}_Q^*) \leftarrow \overline{\mathcal{D}}_{\sigma_0}^{m \times Q\ell},$$

and output  $crs = (pp, \mathbf{R}^*)$ .

Note: The parameters need to satisfy certain relations. We specify them below when a relation is first needed, and set the parameters at the end of the section.

• Enc(crs, x; R): The algorithm on input the crs, and a binary input  $x \in \{0,1\}^K$ , generates the following components.

{42}------------------------------------------------

- *GSW* components:
  - \* Public key hpk =  $\overline{\mathbf{B}} = \begin{pmatrix} \mathbf{B} \\ \mathbf{r}^{\mathsf{T}} \mathbf{B} + \mathbf{e}_{\mathbf{B}}^{\mathsf{T}} \end{pmatrix}$ , where  $m = \Theta(n \log q)$ ,  $\mathbf{r} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_q^n$ ,  $\mathbf{B} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_q^{n \times m}$ ,  $\mathbf{e}_{\mathbf{B}} \leftarrow \overline{\mathcal{D}}_{\sigma}^m$
  - \* Ciphertext hct =  $\overline{\mathbf{B}}\mathbf{R}$  + bits( $\mathbf{r}$ )<sup>T</sup>  $\otimes$   $\mathbf{G}$ , where  $\mathbf{R} \leftarrow \{0,1\}^{m \times n(n+1)\lceil \log q \rceil^2}$
- Connecting components
  - \* Public matrix  $\mathbf{A} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_q^{n \times \ell}$ , where  $\ell$  is an appropriate sublinear quantity in the function output length L as described in Theorem 6.
  - \* Public matrix  $\mathbf{D} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_q^{n \times Qn \lceil \log q \rceil}$ , where  $\mathbf{D} = (\mathbf{D}_1, \dots, \mathbf{D}_Q)$ .
  - \* For  $i \in [Q]$ ,  $\mathbf{c}_i = (\mathbf{s}_i^{\mathsf{T}} \mathbf{A} + \mathbf{e}_i^{\mathsf{T}} \pmod{\Delta})$ , where  $\mathbf{s}_i \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_q^n$ ,  $\mathbf{e}_i \leftarrow \overline{\mathcal{D}}_{\sigma_{\mathbf{e}}}^{\ell}$ .
  - \* For  $i \in [Q]$ ,  $\mathbf{c}_{\mathbf{s},i} = \mathbf{r}^\mathsf{T} \mathbf{D}_i + \mathbf{e}_{\mathbf{s},i}^\mathsf{T} + \mathbf{s}_i^\mathsf{T} \mathbf{G}_n$ , where  $\mathbf{e}_{\mathbf{s},i} \leftarrow \overline{\mathcal{D}}_\sigma^{n\lceil \log q \rceil}$
- Dual GSW components
  - \* Ciphertext for secret key  $dct = \mathbf{U}^{\mathsf{T}}\mathbf{A} + \mathbf{E}_{\mathbf{A}} + \mathbf{I}_{\ell} \otimes \mathbf{G}_{n}^{\mathsf{T}}\mathbf{r}$ , where  $\mathbf{U} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_{q}^{n \times \ell n \lceil \log q \rceil}$ ,  $\mathbf{E}_{\mathbf{A}} \leftarrow \overline{\mathcal{D}}_{\sigma}^{\ell n \lceil \log q \rceil \times \ell}$ .
  - \* Ciphertext for message  $dct_x = \mathbf{W}^T\mathbf{A} + \mathbf{E}_x + \mathbf{x} \otimes \mathbf{G}_{\ell}^T$ , where  $\mathbf{w} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_q^{n \times K\ell\lceil \log q \rceil}$ ,  $\mathbf{E}_x \leftarrow \overline{\mathcal{D}}_{\sigma}^{K\ell\lceil \log q \rceil \times \ell}$ .

The algorithm outputs

$$ct = (hpk, hct, \mathbf{D}, \{\mathbf{c}_i, \mathbf{c}_{\mathbf{s}_i}\}_{i \in [Q]}, \mathbf{A}, dct, dct_{\mathbf{x}}).$$

- Open(crs, g, i, x, R): The algorithm first runs the encryption algorithm Enc(crs, x; R) to recompute all intermediate variables generated in the encryption process as described above, and then computes the opening as follows.
  - 0. Parse function  $g: \{0,1\}^K \to \{0,1\}^L$  as  $g: \{0,1\}^K \to \mathbb{Z}_{2^\kappa}^\ell$ , where every  $\kappa$ -bit chunk of the output is parsed as a  $\kappa$  bit integer in  $[0,2^\kappa-1]$ . Define  $\widetilde{g}: \{0,1\}^K \to \mathbb{Z}_q^\ell$  where  $\widetilde{g}(\mathbf{x}) = p \cdot g(\mathbf{x}) \mod q$ . We require that  $q > 2^\kappa p$ .
  - 1. Homomorphically evaluate the function  $\widetilde{g}$  over the dual-GSW ciphertext  $\operatorname{dct}_x$  to obtain

$$\mathsf{dct}_{\widetilde{g}} = \mathbf{w}_{\widetilde{g}}^{\mathsf{T}} \mathbf{A} + \mathbf{e}_{\widetilde{g}}^{\mathsf{T}} + \widetilde{g}(\mathbf{x})^{\mathsf{T}},$$

where  $\mathbf{w}_{\widetilde{g}}$  is efficiently computable.

2. Homomorphically evaluate function  $f_i$  where  $f_i(\mathbf{r})^{\mathsf{T}} = \Delta \left[ \frac{\mathbf{r}^{\mathsf{T}} \mathbf{D}_i \mathbf{G}^{-1}(\mathbf{A})}{\Delta} \right]$  over the GSW ciphertext hct to obtain

$$hct_{f_i} = \begin{pmatrix} \overline{hct}_{f_i} \\ \underline{hct}_{f_i} \end{pmatrix} = \begin{pmatrix} \mathbf{B}\mathbf{R}_{f_i} \\ (\mathbf{r}^\mathsf{T}\mathbf{B} + \mathbf{e}_{\mathbf{B}}^\mathsf{T})\mathbf{R}_{f_i} + f_i(\mathbf{r})^\mathsf{T} \end{pmatrix}$$

3. Rerandomize  $-hct_{f_i}$  by

$$\begin{pmatrix} \overline{\mathsf{hct}}_i' \\ \underline{\mathsf{hct}}_i' \end{pmatrix} = \mathsf{hct}_i' = \overline{\mathbf{B}} \mathbf{R}_i^* - \mathsf{hct}_{f_i} = \begin{pmatrix} \mathbf{B} \widetilde{\mathbf{R}}_i \\ (\mathbf{r}^\mathsf{T} \mathbf{B} + \mathbf{e}_{\mathbf{B}}^\mathsf{T}) \widetilde{\mathbf{R}}_i - f_i(\mathbf{r})^\mathsf{T} \end{pmatrix},$$

where  $\widetilde{\mathbf{R}}_i = \mathbf{R}_i^* - \mathbf{R}_{f_i}$ .

{43}------------------------------------------------

4. Homomorphically decrypt hot' using dual GSW ciphertext dot by

$$\mathbf{v}_i = \text{vec}(\mathbf{G}^{-1}(-\overline{\text{hct}}_i')), \quad \text{dct}_i = \mathbf{v}_i^{\mathsf{T}} \cdot \text{dct} = \mathbf{u}_i^{\mathsf{T}} \mathbf{A} + \mathbf{e}_i'^{\mathsf{T}} - \mathbf{r}^{\mathsf{T}}(\mathbf{B}\widetilde{\mathbf{R}}_i),$$

where  $\mathbf{u}_{i}^{\mathsf{T}} = \mathbf{v}_{i}^{\mathsf{T}} \mathbf{U}^{\mathsf{T}}$  is efficiently computable.

*Finally, the algorithm outputs the opening*  $\rho_i = \mathbf{u}_i + \mathbf{w}_{\widetilde{g}} + \mathbf{s}_i$ .

• Dec(crs, g, i, ct,  $\rho$ ): The algorithm first parses

$$\operatorname{ct} = (\operatorname{hpk}, \operatorname{hct}, \mathbf{D}, \{\mathbf{c}_i, \mathbf{c}_{\mathbf{s}_i}\}_{i \in [Q]}, \mathbf{A}, \operatorname{dct}, \operatorname{dct}_{\mathbf{x}}).$$

Following the same procedure as the opening algorithm, the decryption algorithm computes

- Dual GSW ciphertext

$$\mathsf{dct}_{\widetilde{g}} = \mathbf{w}_{\widetilde{g}}^{\mathsf{T}} \mathbf{A} + \mathbf{e}_{\widetilde{g}}^{\mathsf{T}} + \widetilde{g}(\mathbf{x})^{\mathsf{T}}.$$

- Rerandomized GSW ciphertext

$$\begin{pmatrix} \overline{\mathsf{hct}}_i' \\ \underline{\mathsf{hct}}_i' \end{pmatrix} = \mathsf{hct}_i' = \begin{pmatrix} \mathbf{B}\widetilde{\mathbf{R}}_i \\ (\mathbf{r}^\mathsf{T}\mathbf{B} + \mathbf{e}_{\mathbf{B}}^\mathsf{T})\widetilde{\mathbf{R}}_i - f_i(\mathbf{r})^\mathsf{T} \end{pmatrix}.$$

- Dual GSW ciphertext

<span id="page-43-1"></span><span id="page-43-0"></span>
$$dct_i = \mathbf{u}_i^{\mathsf{T}} \mathbf{A} + \mathbf{e}_i'^{\mathsf{T}} - \mathbf{r}^{\mathsf{T}} (\mathbf{B} \widetilde{\mathbf{R}}_i).$$

The algorithm approximately decodes  $\widetilde{g}(\mathbf{x})$  by

$$\widetilde{g}(\mathbf{x})^{\mathsf{T}} \approx \widetilde{\mathbf{y}}^{\mathsf{T}} = \underline{\mathsf{hct}}_{i}' + \mathsf{dct}_{i} + \mathsf{dct}_{\widetilde{g}} + \Delta \left[ \frac{\mathbf{c}_{\mathbf{s},i}^{\mathsf{T}} \mathbf{G}^{-1}(\mathbf{A}) - \mathbf{c}_{i}^{\mathsf{T}}}{\Delta} \right] + \mathbf{c}_{i}^{\mathsf{T}} - \rho^{\mathsf{T}} \mathbf{A}.$$
(13)

The algorithm outputs bit string y, which extracted from bits  $(\left|\frac{\tilde{y}}{p}\right|)$ .

<span id="page-43-2"></span>**Theorem 5** (Correctness). Suppose  $\Delta|q$ ,  $m = \Omega(n \log q)$ ,  $q \leq 2^n$ ,  $\sigma_0 \geq m^{\Omega(\log n)}$ ,  $\sigma_{\mathbf{e}} \geq \ell^{\Omega(d)} \sigma \sigma_0$   $\Delta \geq 2^{\lambda} \sigma_{\mathbf{e}}$ , and  $p \geq 8\Delta$ , where m,  $\sigma_0$ ,  $\sigma_{\mathbf{e}}$  are sufficiently large, then Construction 1 is correct. Moreover, the following correctness condition holds with probability  $1 - 2^{-\Omega(\lambda)}$ .

$$\frac{\operatorname{hct}_{i}' + \operatorname{dct}_{i} + \operatorname{dct}_{\widetilde{g}} + \Delta \left[ \frac{\mathbf{c}_{\mathbf{s},i}^{\mathsf{T}} \mathbf{G}^{-1}(\mathbf{A}) - \mathbf{c}_{i}^{\mathsf{T}}}{\Delta} \right] + \mathbf{c}_{i}^{\mathsf{T}} - \rho^{\mathsf{T}} \mathbf{A} = \widetilde{g}(\mathbf{x})^{\mathsf{T}} + \widetilde{\mathbf{e}}_{i}^{\mathsf{T}}$$

$$\widetilde{\mathbf{e}}^{\mathsf{T}} = \mathbf{e}_{\mathbf{B}}^{\mathsf{T}} \widetilde{\mathbf{R}}_{i} + \mathbf{e}_{\widetilde{g}}^{\mathsf{T}} + \mathbf{e}_{i}^{\mathsf{T}} + \mathbf{e}_{i}^{\mathsf{T}}$$
(14)

*Proof.* First observe that in the decryption equation 13, the connecting components satisfy

$$\Delta \cdot \left[ \frac{\mathbf{c}_{\mathbf{s},i}^{\mathsf{T}} \mathbf{G}^{-1}(\mathbf{A}) - \mathbf{c}_{i}^{\mathsf{T}}}{\Delta} \right] + \mathbf{c}_{i}^{\mathsf{T}} = \Delta \cdot \left[ \frac{\mathbf{r}^{\mathsf{T}} \mathbf{D}_{i} \mathbf{G}^{-1}(\mathbf{A}) + \mathbf{e}_{\mathbf{s},i}^{\mathsf{T}} \mathbf{G}^{-1}(\mathbf{A}) + \mathbf{s}_{i}^{\mathsf{T}} \mathbf{A} - (\mathbf{s}_{i}^{\mathsf{T}} \mathbf{A} + \mathbf{e}_{i}^{\mathsf{T}} \bmod \Delta)}{\Delta} \right] + \mathbf{c}_{i}^{\mathsf{T}}$$

$$= \Delta \cdot \left[ \frac{\mathbf{r}^{\mathsf{T}} \mathbf{D}_{i} \mathbf{G}^{-1}(\mathbf{A}) + \mathbf{e}_{\mathbf{s},i}^{\mathsf{T}} \mathbf{G}^{-1}(\mathbf{A}) - \mathbf{e}_{i}^{\mathsf{T}}}{\Delta} + \frac{\mathbf{s}_{i}^{\mathsf{T}} \mathbf{A} + \mathbf{e}_{i}^{\mathsf{T}} - (\mathbf{s}_{i}^{\mathsf{T}} \mathbf{A} + \mathbf{e}_{i}^{\mathsf{T}} \bmod \Delta)}{\Delta} \right] + \mathbf{c}_{i}^{\mathsf{T}}$$

$$= \Delta \cdot \left[ \frac{\mathbf{r}^{\mathsf{T}} \mathbf{D}_{i} \mathbf{G}^{-1}(\mathbf{A}) + \mathbf{e}_{\mathbf{s},i}^{\mathsf{T}} \mathbf{G}^{-1}(\mathbf{A}) - \mathbf{e}_{i}^{\mathsf{T}}}{\Delta} \right] + \Delta \cdot \left[ \frac{\mathbf{s}_{i}^{\mathsf{T}} \mathbf{A} + \mathbf{e}_{i}^{\mathsf{T}}}{\Delta} \right] + (\mathbf{s}_{i}^{\mathsf{T}} \mathbf{A} + \mathbf{e}_{i}^{\mathsf{T}} \bmod \Delta)$$

$$= \Delta \cdot \left[ \frac{\mathbf{r}^{\mathsf{T}} \mathbf{D}_{i} \mathbf{G}^{-1}(\mathbf{A}) + \mathbf{e}_{\mathbf{s},i}^{\mathsf{T}} \mathbf{G}^{-1}(\mathbf{A}) - \mathbf{e}_{i}^{\mathsf{T}}}{\Delta} \right] + \mathbf{s}_{i}^{\mathsf{T}} \mathbf{A} + \mathbf{e}_{i}^{\mathsf{T}}.$$

{44}------------------------------------------------

Therefore, by expanding the decryption equation, we get

$$\widetilde{\mathbf{y}}^{\mathsf{T}} = (\mathbf{r}^{\mathsf{T}}\mathbf{B} + \mathbf{e}_{\mathbf{B}}^{\mathsf{T}})\widetilde{\mathbf{R}}_{i} - \Delta \left[ \frac{\mathbf{r}^{\mathsf{T}}\mathbf{D}_{i}\mathbf{G}^{-1}(\mathbf{A})}{\Delta} \right] + \mathbf{w}_{\widetilde{g}}^{\mathsf{T}}\mathbf{A} + \mathbf{e}_{\widetilde{g}}^{\mathsf{T}} + \widetilde{g}(\mathbf{x})^{\mathsf{T}} + \mathbf{u}_{i}^{\mathsf{T}}\mathbf{A} + \mathbf{e}_{i}^{\mathsf{T}} - \mathbf{r}^{\mathsf{T}}(\mathbf{B}\widetilde{\mathbf{R}}_{i}) \right] 
+ \Delta \cdot \left[ \frac{\mathbf{r}^{\mathsf{T}}\mathbf{D}_{i}\mathbf{G}^{-1}(\mathbf{A}) + \mathbf{e}_{\mathbf{s},i}^{\mathsf{T}}\mathbf{G}^{-1}(\mathbf{A}) - \mathbf{e}_{i}^{\mathsf{T}}}{\Delta} \right] + \mathbf{s}_{i}^{\mathsf{T}}\mathbf{A} + \mathbf{e}_{i}^{\mathsf{T}} - (\mathbf{u}_{i} + \mathbf{w}_{\widetilde{g}} + \mathbf{s}_{i})^{\mathsf{T}}\mathbf{A} 
= \widetilde{g}(\mathbf{x})^{\mathsf{T}} + \mathbf{e}_{\mathbf{B}}^{\mathsf{T}}\widetilde{\mathbf{R}}_{i} + \mathbf{e}_{\widetilde{g}}^{\mathsf{T}} + \mathbf{e}_{i}^{\mathsf{T}} + \mathbf{e}_{i}^{\mathsf{T}} + \Delta\eta_{i},$$

$$(15)$$

$$\text{where } \eta_{i} = \left( \left[ \frac{\mathbf{r}^{\mathsf{T}}\mathbf{D}_{i}\mathbf{G}^{-1}(\mathbf{A}) + \mathbf{e}_{\mathbf{s},i}^{\mathsf{T}}\mathbf{G}^{-1}(\mathbf{A}) - \mathbf{e}_{i}^{\mathsf{T}}}{\Delta} \right] - \left[ \frac{\mathbf{r}^{\mathsf{T}}\mathbf{D}_{i}\mathbf{G}^{-1}(\mathbf{A})}{\Delta} \right] \right).$$

The error terms in the above equation are bounded by

<span id="page-44-1"></span>
$$\begin{aligned} \left\| \mathbf{e}_{\mathbf{B}}^{\mathsf{T}} \widetilde{\mathbf{R}}_{i} \right\| &\leq \left\| \mathbf{e}_{\mathbf{B}}^{\mathsf{T}} \mathbf{R}_{f_{i}} \right\| + \left\| \mathbf{e}_{\mathbf{B}}^{\mathsf{T}} \mathbf{R}_{i}^{*} \right\| \leq \sigma \sqrt{\lambda} \cdot m \cdot (m^{O(\log n)} + \sigma_{0} \sqrt{\lambda}) \leq 2m \lambda \sigma \sigma_{0}, \\ \left\| \mathbf{e}_{\widetilde{g}} \right\| &\leq \ell^{O(d)} \sigma \sqrt{\lambda} \leq \sigma_{\mathbf{e}}, \quad , \left\| \mathbf{e}_{i}^{\prime} \right\| \leq \ell n \sigma \sqrt{\lambda}, \quad \left\| \mathbf{e}_{i} \right\| \leq \sigma_{\mathbf{e}}, \\ \left| \eta_{i} \right| &\leq 1 \text{ since } \left\| \mathbf{e}_{\mathbf{s},i}^{\mathsf{T}} \mathbf{G}^{-1}(\mathbf{A}) - \mathbf{e}_{i}^{\mathsf{T}} \right\| \leq \Delta + m \sigma \sqrt{\lambda} + \sigma_{\mathbf{e}} \sqrt{\lambda} \leq \Delta \end{aligned}$$

The norm bound  $\|\mathbf{R}_{f_i}\| = m^{O(\log n)}$  follows from the observation that the function  $f_i$  can be computed by a circuit of depth  $O(\log(n \log q)) = O(\log n)$ . Therefore, the decoding error of  $\tilde{\mathbf{y}}$  has norm bound

$$\left\| \left\lfloor \frac{\tilde{\mathbf{y}}}{p} \right\rfloor - \left\lfloor \frac{\tilde{g}(\mathbf{x})}{p} \right\rfloor \right\| = \left\| \left\lfloor \frac{\tilde{\mathbf{y}} - \tilde{g}(\mathbf{x})}{p} \right\rfloor \right\| \le \left\lfloor \frac{5\sigma_{\mathbf{e}} + \Delta}{p} \right\rfloor \le \left\lfloor \frac{1}{4} \right\rfloor = 0,$$

where the first equation follows from the fact that  $\tilde{g}(\mathbf{x})$  is always a multiple of p. Therefore,  $\left\lfloor \frac{\tilde{\mathbf{y}}}{p} \right\rfloor = \left\lfloor \frac{\tilde{g}(\mathbf{x})}{p} \right\rfloor$ , indicating that the decryption algorithm recovers  $g(\mathbf{x})$  perfectly. Moreover, by the observation that

$$\left\|\mathbf{e}_{\mathbf{s},i}^{\mathsf{T}}\mathbf{G}^{-1}(\mathbf{A}) - \mathbf{e}_{i}^{\mathsf{T}}\right\| \leq \Delta + m\sigma\sqrt{\lambda} + \sigma_{\mathbf{e}}\sqrt{\lambda} \leq 2^{-\Omega(\lambda)}\Delta,$$

along with the fact that  $\mathbf{r}^{\mathsf{T}}\mathbf{D}_{i}\mathbf{G}^{-1}(\mathbf{A})$  is marginally random, the rounding lemma guarantees that with probability  $1 - 2^{-\Omega(\lambda)}$ ,

$$\left| \frac{\mathbf{r}^{\mathsf{T}} \mathbf{D}_{i} \mathbf{G}^{-1}(\mathbf{A}) + \mathbf{e}_{\mathbf{s},i}^{\mathsf{T}} \mathbf{G}^{-1}(\mathbf{A}) - \mathbf{e}_{i}^{\mathsf{T}}}{\Delta} \right| = \left| \frac{\mathbf{r}^{\mathsf{T}} \mathbf{D}_{i} \mathbf{G}^{-1}(\mathbf{A})}{\Delta} \right|.$$

Therefore  $\eta_i = 0$  with overwhelming probability. Hence, combining the decryption equation (13) with equation (15), we conclude that the equation (14) holds with overwhelming probability.

<span id="page-44-0"></span>**Theorem 6** (Succinctness). Construction 1 is succinct if there exists constants  $\alpha$ ,  $\beta$ ,  $\gamma \in (0,1)$  such that  $n \leq L^{\alpha} \cdot \mathsf{poly}(\lambda, k, d)$ ,  $\kappa \leq L^{\beta}$ ,  $\ell \leq L^{\gamma}$  where  $\beta + \gamma \geq 1$  and  $\alpha + \beta < 1/2$ ,  $m = \Theta(n \log q)$ ,  $q = 2^{\Theta(\kappa)}p$ , and parameters  $(\log \Delta, \log p) = \mathsf{poly}(\lambda, K, d, \log L)$ .

*Proof.* The size of the opening is bounded by

$$|\rho_i| = n \log q = n(\log p + O(\kappa)) = L^{\alpha+\beta} \operatorname{poly}(\lambda, K, d),$$

{45}------------------------------------------------

where  $\alpha + \beta < 1/2$ . For the encoding, we can separate the components into *Q*-dependent and *Q*-independent terms. The *Q* independent terms have size bounded by

$$|\mathsf{hpk}|, |\mathsf{hct}|, |\mathsf{A}|, |\mathsf{dct}|, |\mathsf{dct}_{\mathsf{x}}| = \mathsf{poly}(n, m, K, \ell, \log q) = \mathsf{poly}(L) \cdot \mathsf{poly}(\lambda, K, d).$$

On the other hand, the *Q*-dependent terms have size bounded by

$$|\mathbf{D}| = Qnm \log q \le QL^{2\alpha + 2\beta} \cdot \operatorname{poly}(\lambda, K, d),$$

$$|\{\mathbf{c}_{\mathbf{s},i}\}_{i \in Q}| = Qm \log q \le QL^{\alpha + 2\beta} \cdot \operatorname{poly}(\lambda, K, d),$$

$$|\{\mathbf{c}_{i}\}_{i \in Q}| = Q\ell \log \Delta \le QL^{\gamma} \cdot \operatorname{poly}(\lambda, K, d).$$

Therefore the overall size of the encoding is bounded by  $(QL^{1-\epsilon} + \mathsf{poly}(L)) \cdot \mathsf{poly}(\lambda, K, d)$  for constant  $\epsilon = 1 - \max(2(\alpha + \beta), \gamma)$ .

**Theorem 7** (SIM-security). Assuming  $n = \text{poly}(\lambda)$ ,  $q < 2^n$ ,  $m = \Omega(n \log q)$ ,  $\sigma_0 \ge 2^{\lambda} m^{\Omega(\log n)} \sigma$ ,  $\sigma_{\mathbf{e}} \ge 2^{\lambda} \sigma \sigma_0 \ell^{\Omega(\log n+d)}$ , and  $\Delta \ge 2^{\lambda} \ell^{\Omega(d)} \sigma \sigma_0$ , where m,  $\sigma_0$ ,  $\sigma_{\mathbf{e}}$ ,  $\Delta$  are sufficiently large, and assuming that the CRO assumption (assumption 1) is (sub-exponentially) secure for parameters  $(n, q, \Delta, \sigma)$ , then construction 1 is (sub-exponentially) SIM-secure.

*Proof.* We consider the following sequence of hybrids. We inline intuition on why neighboring hybrids are indistinguishable and provide formal proofs after all hybrids are described.

•  $\mathcal{H}_0$ : This is the LHS of the SIM-security definition in definition 10. For message-function tuple  $(\mathbf{x}, g_1, \dots, g_n)$ , the output distribution of this hybrid is described by

$$\begin{cases} (\operatorname{crs},\operatorname{ct},\{\rho_i\}_{i\in[Q]}) & \operatorname{crs} & \leftarrow \operatorname{Gen}(1^{\lambda},1^{Q},1^{k},1^{L},1^{d}) \\ \operatorname{ct} & \leftarrow \operatorname{Enc}(\operatorname{crs},\mathbf{x};R) \\ \rho_i & \leftarrow \operatorname{Open}(\operatorname{crs},g_i,i,\mathbf{x},R) \end{cases}$$

- $\mathcal{H}_1$ : Same as  $\mathcal{H}_0$ , except that in all algorithms, the samples from the bounded discrete Gaussian  $\overline{\mathcal{D}}$  are replaced with samples from the standard discrete Gaussian  $\mathcal{D}$ . Hybrid  $\mathcal{H}_1$  is statistically close to  $\mathcal{H}_0$  following the fact that Gaussian distributions have small tails (Lemma 2).
- $\mathcal{H}_2$ : Same as  $\mathcal{H}_1$ , but in the encryption algorithm, the randomness  $\mathbf{s}_i$ ,  $\mathbf{e}_i$  for the connecting components are computed differently. The hybrid first samples

$$\tilde{\mathbf{s}}_i \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_a^n$$
,  $\tilde{\mathbf{e}}_i \leftarrow \mathcal{D}_{\sigma_a}^\ell$ 

then programs

$$\mathbf{s}_i = \widetilde{\mathbf{s}}_i - \mathbf{u}_i - \mathbf{w}_{\widetilde{g}_i}, \quad \mathbf{e}_i^{\mathsf{T}} = \widetilde{\mathbf{e}}_i - \mathbf{e}_{\mathbf{B}}^{\mathsf{T}} \widetilde{\mathbf{R}}_i - \mathbf{e}_i^{\mathsf{T}} - \mathbf{e}_{\widetilde{\sigma}_i}^{\mathsf{T}}.$$

Note that the opening  $\rho_i = \tilde{\mathbf{s}}_i$  for all  $i \in [Q]$ . Hybrid  $\mathcal{H}_2$  is statistically close to  $\mathcal{H}_1$  because the marginal distribution of  $\tilde{\mathbf{s}}_i$ ,  $\tilde{\mathbf{e}}_i$  in  $\mathcal{H}_1$  is uniformly random over  $\mathbb{Z}_q$  and statistically close to i.i.d. Gaussian  $\mathcal{D}_{\sigma_e}$ . Therefore, it is statistically close to sample them first, and then reverse compute  $\mathbf{s}_i$  and  $\mathbf{e}_i$ . See Lemma 8.

•  $\mathcal{H}_3$ : Same as  $\mathcal{H}_2$ , but in the encryption algorithm, the connecting components are computed differently. The hybrid sets

$$\mathbf{c}_i^{\mathsf{T}} = (\widetilde{\mathbf{s}}_i^{\mathsf{T}} \mathbf{A} + \widetilde{\mathbf{e}}_i^{\mathsf{T}} - \mathsf{dct}_{f_i} - \underline{\mathsf{hct}}_i' - \mathsf{dct}_{\widetilde{g}_i} + \widetilde{g}(\mathbf{x})^{\mathsf{T}} \bmod \Delta).$$

{46}------------------------------------------------

For elements  $\mathbf{c}_{\mathbf{s},i}$ , the hybrid first computes intermediate elements

$$\widehat{\mathbf{c}}_{i}^{\mathsf{T}} = \mathbf{r}^{\mathsf{T}} \mathbf{D}_{i} + \mathbf{e}_{\mathbf{s},i}^{\mathsf{T}} - \mathbf{u}_{i}^{\mathsf{T}} \mathbf{G} = \mathbf{r}^{\mathsf{T}} \mathbf{D}_{i} + \mathbf{e}_{\mathbf{s},i}^{\mathsf{T}} - \text{vec}(\mathbf{G}^{-1}(-\overline{\mathsf{hct}}_{i}')) \cdot \mathbf{U}^{\mathsf{T}} \mathbf{G}$$

then set  $\mathbf{c}_{\mathbf{s},i}^{\mathsf{T}} = \widehat{\mathbf{c}}_{i}^{\mathsf{T}} + \widetilde{\mathbf{s}}_{i}^{\mathsf{T}}\mathbf{G} - \mathbf{w}_{\widetilde{g}_{i}}\mathbf{G}$ . Note that  $\mathbf{w}_{\widetilde{g}_{i}}$  is efficiently computable given secret  $\mathbf{W}$ , ciphertext,  $\mathsf{dct}_{\mathbf{x}}$ , function  $g_{i}$ , and message  $\mathbf{x}$ .

Hybrid  $\mathcal{H}_3$  and  $\mathcal{H}_2$  are identically distributed. The emulation of  $\mathbf{c}_i^{\mathsf{T}}$  is perfect following from the correctness condition Equation (14) in Theorem 5. The emulation of  $\mathbf{c}_{s,i}$  is also perfect because  $\mathbf{c}_{s,i}$  is supposed to encode  $\mathbf{s}_i \mathbf{G}$  which by the programming step in  $\mathcal{H}_2$  equals to  $(\tilde{\mathbf{s}}_i - \mathbf{u}_i - \mathbf{w}_{\tilde{\mathbf{g}}_i})\mathbf{G}$ .

•  $\mathcal{H}_4$ : Same as  $\mathcal{H}_3$ , but in the generation of crs, the hybrid samples  $\mathbf{R}^*$  indirectly. Namely, the algorithm first sample  $\mathbf{R}_0 = (\mathbf{R}_{0,1}, \dots, \mathbf{R}_{0,Q}) \leftarrow \mathcal{D}_{\sigma_0}^{m \times Q\ell}$ , compute ciphertexts  $\mathsf{hct}_{0,i} = \overline{\mathbf{B}} \mathbf{R}_{0,i}$  for all  $i \in [Q]$ , then reverse sample  $\mathbf{R}^*$  from the conditional distribution

$$\mathbf{R}_i^* \leftarrow \mathcal{D}_{\sigma_0}^{m \times \ell}|_{\overline{\mathbf{B}}\mathbf{R}_i^* = \mathsf{hct}_{0,i}}.$$

Note that in this hybrid, the GSW rerandomization can be written by

$$hct'_i = hct_{0,i} - hct_{f_i}$$

therefore one can equivalently write the reverse sample of  $\mathbf{R}^*$  by

$$\mathbf{R}_{i}^{*} \leftarrow \mathcal{D}_{\sigma_{0}}^{m \times \ell}|_{\mathbf{\overline{B}R}_{i}^{*} = \mathsf{hct}_{i}' + \mathsf{hct}_{f_{i}}}$$

Hybrid  $\mathcal{H}_4$  is identically distributed to  $\mathcal{H}_3$  since it only changes the order of sampling to hct<sub>0</sub> first and  $\mathbf{R}^*$  second, and replaces hct<sub>0</sub> using equality.

•  $\mathcal{H}_5$ : Same as  $\mathcal{H}_4$ , but rewrites the GSW rerandomization equation by

$$hct'_i = hct_{0,i} \boxminus f_i(\mathbf{r})$$

Notice that this implies  $\overline{\mathsf{hct}}_i' = \overline{\mathsf{hct}}_{0,i}$ . The sampling of  $\mathbf{R}^*$  is subsequently replaced by

$$\mathbf{R}_{i}^{*} \leftarrow \mathcal{D}_{\sigma_{0}}^{m \times \ell} |_{\mathbf{B}\mathbf{R}_{i}^{*} = \mathsf{hct}_{f_{i}} + \mathsf{hct}_{0,i} \boxminus f_{i}(\mathbf{r})}$$

Hybrid  $\mathcal{H}_5$  is statistically close to  $\mathcal{H}_4$  because by the re-randomizability of GSW,  $hct_{0,i} = f_i(\mathbf{r})$  is statistically close to  $hct_{0,i} - hct_{f_i}$ . The former is a fresh encryption of  $f_i(\mathbf{r})$  using wide Gaussian  $\mathcal{D}_{\sigma_0}$  and the latter is a re-randomized encryption of  $f_i(\mathbf{r})$ .

•  $\mathcal{H}_6$ : Define function  $\widetilde{f_i}$  as

$$\widetilde{f_i}(\mathsf{hct},\mathsf{hct}_{0,i},\mathbf{A},\mathbf{D}_i,\mathsf{dct},\widehat{\mathbf{c}}_i)^{\mathsf{T}} = \Delta \left| \frac{\widehat{\mathbf{c}}_i^{\mathsf{T}}\mathbf{G}^{-1}(\mathbf{A}) + \mathsf{vec}(\mathbf{G}^{-1}(-\overline{\mathsf{hct}}_{0,i}))^{\mathsf{T}} \cdot \mathsf{dct} + \underline{\mathsf{hct}}_{0,i}}{\Delta} \right|,$$

and replace  $f_i(\mathbf{r})$  by  $\widetilde{f_i}(\mathsf{hct}, \mathsf{hct}_{0,i}, \mathbf{A}, \mathbf{D}_i, \mathsf{dct}, \widehat{\mathbf{c}}_i)$  in the sampling equation of  $\mathbf{R}_i^*$ , namely,

$$\mathbf{R}_i^* \leftarrow \mathcal{D}_{\sigma_0}^{m \times \ell}|_{\overline{\mathbf{B}}\mathbf{R}_i^* = \mathsf{hct}_{f_i} + \mathsf{hct}_{0,i} \boxminus \widetilde{f_i}(\mathsf{hct}, \mathsf{hct}_{0,i}, \mathbf{A}, \mathbf{D}_i, \mathsf{dct}, \mathbf{c}_{\mathbf{u},i})}^{m \times \ell}.$$

All other variables are sampled as in  $\mathcal{H}_5$ .

{47}------------------------------------------------

Hybrid  $\mathcal{H}_6$  is statistically close to  $\mathcal{H}_5$  because  $f_i(\mathbf{r}) = \widetilde{f_i}(\mathsf{hct}, \mathsf{hct}_{0,i}, \mathbf{A}, \mathbf{D}_i, \mathsf{dct}, \widehat{\mathbf{c}}_i)$  with overwhelming probability, which follows from arguments similar to claim 1. See Lemma 12.

Observe that in  $\mathcal{H}_6$ , the sampling of (hpk, hct, hct<sub>0</sub>,  $\mathbf{A}$ ,  $\mathbf{D}$ , dct,  $\widehat{\mathbf{c}}$ ) matches that of (hpk, hct, hct<sub>0</sub>,  $\mathbf{A}$ ,  $\mathbf{D}$ , ct<sub>1</sub>, ct<sub>2</sub>) in the real distribution  $\mathcal{D}_0$  of the CRO assumption, Assumption 1. In particular, dct = ct<sub>1</sub> and  $\widehat{\mathbf{c}}$  encrypts the same circular message as ct<sub>2</sub>,  $\mathbf{u}_i = f^{\mathrm{circ}}(\mathbf{U}, \mathrm{hct_0}) = -\mathrm{vec}(\mathbf{G}^{-1}(-\overline{\mathrm{hct_i}})) \cdot \mathbf{U}^{\mathsf{T}}\mathbf{G}$ , given  $\overline{\mathrm{hct_i}} = \overline{\mathrm{hct_i'}}$ . The function  $f_i(\mathbf{r})$  is the same as described in the CRO assumption, and the above function  $\widehat{f_i}$  computes  $f_i$  using public encodings, corresponding to the safety constraint in the CRO assumption.

•  $\mathcal{H}_7$ : This hybrid samples the following components as random.

(hpk, hct, dct, {hct<sub>0,i</sub>, 
$$\widehat{\mathbf{c}}_i$$
} <sub>$i \in [Q]$</sub> )  $\leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_q^{(n+1) \times m} \times \mathbb{Z}_q^{(n+1) \times n(n+1) \lceil \log q \rceil^2} \times \mathbb{Z}_q^{\ell n \lceil \log q \rceil \times \ell} \times (\mathbb{Z}_q^{(n+1) \times \ell} \times \mathbb{Z}_q^{n \lceil \log q \rceil})^Q$ , and compute/sample the remaining elements as in  $\mathcal{H}_6$ .

Hybrid  $\mathcal{H}_7$  is computationally indistinguishable to  $\mathcal{H}_6$  following the CRO assumption (Assumption 1) w.r.t. parameters  $(n, q, \Delta, \sigma)$ . As sketched in Hybrid  $\mathcal{H}_6$  and as detailed in Lemma 13, the real and ideal distribution of CRO matches exactly  $\mathcal{H}_6$  and  $\mathcal{H}_7$ .

•  $\mathcal{H}_8$ : Same as  $\mathcal{H}_7$ , except that the GSW public key is sampled with trapdoor (lemma 5), namely,

$$(hpk = \overline{\mathbf{B}}, \mathbf{T}) \leftarrow TrapGen(1^{n+1}, 1^m).$$

Hybrid  $\mathcal{H}_8$  and  $\mathcal{H}_7$  are statistically close by properties of lattice trapdoor sampling.

•  $\mathcal{H}_9$ : Same as  $\mathcal{H}_8$ , except that the conditional sampling of  $\mathbf{R}^*$  is replaced by the efficient procedure

$$\mathbf{R}_i^* \leftarrow \mathsf{SampPre}(\mathbf{A}, \mathbf{T}, (\mathsf{hct}_{f_i} + \mathsf{hct}_{0,i} \boxminus \widetilde{f_i}(\mathsf{hct}, \mathsf{hct}_{0,i}, \mathbf{A}, \mathbf{D}_i, \mathsf{dct}, \widehat{\mathbf{c}}_i)), \sigma_0)$$

Hybrid  $\mathcal{H}_8$  and  $\mathcal{H}_7$  are statistically close by properties of preimage sampling using lattice trapdoors.

- $\mathcal{H}_{10}$ : Same as  $\mathcal{H}_{9}$ , except now  $\mathbf{c}_{\mathbf{s},i} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_{q}^{m}$  are sampled at random, while  $\widehat{\mathbf{c}}_{i}^{\mathsf{T}} = \mathbf{c}_{\mathbf{s},i}^{\mathsf{T}} \widetilde{\mathbf{s}}_{i}^{\mathsf{T}}\mathbf{G} + \mathbf{w}_{\widetilde{g}_{i}}^{\mathsf{T}}\mathbf{G}$ . Hybrid  $\mathcal{H}_{10}$  is identically distributed as  $\mathcal{H}_{9}$ , since in the latter  $\widehat{\mathbf{c}}_{i} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_{q}^{m}$  and  $\mathbf{c}_{\mathbf{s},i}^{\mathsf{T}} = \widehat{\mathbf{c}}_{i} + \widetilde{\mathbf{s}}_{i}^{\mathsf{T}}\mathbf{G} - \mathbf{w}_{\widetilde{g}_{i}}^{\mathsf{T}}\mathbf{G}$ .
- $\mathcal{H}_{11}$ : Define function  $\widetilde{f}'_i$  as

$$\begin{split} &\widetilde{f}_i'(\mathsf{hct},\mathsf{hct}_{0,i},\mathbf{A},\mathbf{D}_i,\mathsf{dct},\mathsf{dct}_{\mathbf{x}},\mathbf{c}_{\mathbf{s},i},\widetilde{\mathbf{s}}_i,\widetilde{g}_i(\mathbf{x}))^\mathsf{T} \\ = &\Delta \left| \frac{\mathbf{c}_{\mathbf{s},i}^\mathsf{T}\mathbf{G}^{-1}(\mathbf{A}) - \widetilde{\mathbf{s}}_i^\mathsf{T}\mathbf{A} + \mathsf{dct}_{\widetilde{g}_i}^\mathsf{T} - \widetilde{g}_i(\mathbf{x})^\mathsf{T} + \mathsf{vec}(\mathbf{G}^{-1}(-\overline{\mathsf{hct}}_{0,i}))^\mathsf{T} \cdot \mathsf{dct} + \underline{\mathsf{hct}}_{0,i}}{\Delta} \right|, \end{split}$$

and replace  $\widetilde{f_i}$  (hct, hct<sub>0,i</sub>,  $\mathbf{A}$ ,  $\mathbf{D}_i$ , dct, dct<sub>x</sub>,  $\widehat{\mathbf{c}}_i$ ) by  $\widetilde{f_i}'$  (hct, hct<sub>0,i</sub>,  $\mathbf{A}$ ,  $\mathbf{D}_i$ , dct,  $\mathbf{c}_{\mathbf{s},i}$ ,  $\widetilde{\mathbf{s}}_i$ ,  $\widetilde{g}_i(\mathbf{x})$ ) in the preimage sampling equation, namely,

$$\mathbf{R}_{i}^{*} \leftarrow \mathsf{SampPre}(\mathbf{A}, \mathbf{T}, (\mathsf{hct}_{f_{i}} + \mathsf{hct}_{0, i} \boxminus \widetilde{f}_{i}'(\mathsf{hct}, \mathsf{hct}_{0, i}, \mathbf{A}, \mathbf{D}_{i}, \mathsf{dct}, \mathsf{dct}_{\mathbf{x}}, \mathbf{c}_{\mathbf{s}, i}, \widetilde{\mathbf{s}}_{i}, \widetilde{g}_{i}(\mathbf{x}))), \sigma_{0})$$

All other elements are sampled the same as  $\mathcal{H}_{10}$ . Hybrid  $\mathcal{H}_{11}$  is statistically close to  $\mathcal{H}_{10}$ , following from the fact that  $\hat{\mathbf{c}}_i^\mathsf{T} \mathbf{G}^{-1}(\mathbf{A}) = \mathbf{c}_{\mathbf{s},i}^\mathsf{T} \mathbf{G}^{-1}(\mathbf{A}) - \tilde{\mathbf{s}}_i^\mathsf{T} \mathbf{A} + \mathsf{dct}_{\widetilde{g}_i}^\mathsf{T} - \widetilde{g}_i(\mathbf{x})^\mathsf{T} - \mathbf{e}_{\widetilde{g}_i}^\mathsf{T}$ , and the last error term does not affect rounding result with overwhelming probability.

{48}------------------------------------------------

Note that in this hybrid, the intermediate terms  $\hat{\mathbf{c}}_i$  are no longer needed. Therefore, the hybrid does not need to compute the secret  $\mathbf{w}_{\widetilde{g}_i}$  and the ciphertext  $\mathsf{dct}_x$  is the only term directly dependent on the secret  $\mathbf{W}$ .

•  $\mathcal{H}_{12}$ : Same as  $\mathcal{H}_{11}$ , except now  $dct_x$  is sampled at random. Hybrid  $\mathcal{H}_{12}$  is computationally indistinguishable to  $\mathcal{H}_{11}$  following the LWE assumption, since  $dct_x$  is a fresh dual-GSW encryption of x using secret w that is not used for the rest of sampling of  $\mathcal{H}_{11}$ .

 $\mathcal{H}_{12}$  is the RHS of the SIM-security definition in definition 10, where every term is efficiently simulatable given  $g_i$  and  $g_i(\mathbf{x})$ . For full exposure, we describe the simulator as follows.

 $Sim(1^{\lambda}, \{g_i, g_i(\mathbf{x})\}_{i \in [Q]})$ :

- Set parameters pp as in  $Gen(1^{\lambda}, 1^{Q}, 1^{K}, 1^{L}, 1^{d})$ .
- Sample public key (hpk =  $\overline{\mathbf{B}}$ ,  $\mathbf{T}$ )  $\leftarrow$  TrapGen( $1^{n+1}$ ,  $1^m$ ).
- Sample elements  $(\tilde{\mathbf{s}}_i, \tilde{\mathbf{e}}_i, \mathsf{hct}, \mathsf{hct}_{0,i}, \mathsf{dct}, \mathsf{dct}_{\mathbf{x}}, \mathbf{c}_{\mathbf{s},i}) \leftarrow \$$ .
- Compute  $\mathbf{c}_i^{\mathsf{T}} = (\tilde{\mathbf{s}}_i^{\mathsf{T}} + \tilde{\mathbf{e}}_i^{\mathsf{T}} \mathsf{dct}_{f_i} \mathsf{hct}_i^* \mathsf{dct}_{\widetilde{g}_i} + \widetilde{g}_i(\mathbf{x})^{\mathsf{T}} \bmod \Delta).$
- Sample  $\mathbf{R}_{i}^{*} \leftarrow \mathsf{SampPre}(\mathbf{A}, \mathbf{T}, (\mathsf{hct}_{f_{i}} + \mathsf{hct}_{0,i} \boxminus \widetilde{f}_{i}'(\mathsf{hct}, \mathsf{hct}_{0,i}, \mathbf{A}, \mathbf{D}_{i}, \mathsf{dct}, \mathsf{dct}_{\mathbf{x}}, \mathbf{c}_{\mathbf{s},i}, \widetilde{g}_{i}(\mathbf{x}))), \sigma_{0}).$
- Output crs = (pp,  $\mathbb{R}^*$ ), ct = (hpk, hct,  $\mathbb{D}$ , { $\mathbf{c}_i$ ,  $\mathbf{c}_{\mathbf{s}_i}$ } $_{i \in [Q]}$ ,  $\mathbb{A}$ , dct, dct<sub>x</sub>), and  $\rho_i = \tilde{\mathbf{s}}_i$  for all  $i \in [Q]$ .

Next, we formally argue the indistinguishability between neighboring hybrids.

<span id="page-48-1"></span>**Lemma 7.** The statistical distance between  $\mathcal{H}_0$  and  $\mathcal{H}_1$  is bounded by  $2^{-\Omega(\lambda)}$ .

*Proof.* This follows directly from Lemma 2, which states that each sample from  $\overline{\mathcal{D}}$  is  $2^{-\lambda}$ -close to sample  $\mathcal{D}$ .

<span id="page-48-0"></span>**Lemma 8.** If  $\sigma_0 \ge m^{O(\log n)}$  and  $\sigma_{\mathbf{e}} = 2^{\lambda} \cdot \sigma \sigma_0 \ell^{\Omega(\log n + d)}$ , the statistical distance between  $\mathcal{H}_1$  and  $\mathcal{H}_2$  is bounded by  $2^{-\Omega(\lambda)}$ .

*Proof.* It is easy to observe that the distribution of  $\mathbf{s}_i$  is uniformly random in both hybrids. For the distribution of  $\mathbf{e}_i$ , observe that with probability  $2^{-\Omega(\lambda)}$ ,

$$\left\|\mathbf{e}_{\mathbf{B}}^{\mathsf{T}}\widetilde{\mathbf{R}}_{i}-\mathbf{e}_{i}^{\mathsf{T}}-\mathbf{e}_{\widetilde{g}_{i}}^{\mathsf{T}}\right\| \leq \sigma\sqrt{\lambda}\cdot m\cdot (m^{O(\log n)}+\sigma_{0}\sqrt{\lambda})+\ell n\sigma\sqrt{\lambda}+\ell^{O(d)}\sigma\sqrt{\lambda} \leq \mathsf{poly}(\lambda)\sigma\sigma_{0}\ell^{O(\log n+d)},$$

where the analysis is identical to the proof of Theorem 5. Thus, following the smudging lemma (lemma 3), the statistical distance between  $\mathbf{e}_i \leftarrow \mathcal{D}_{\sigma_\mathbf{e}}^\ell$  and  $\mathbf{e}_i \leftarrow \mathcal{D}_{\sigma_\mathbf{e}}^\ell + (\mathbf{e}_\mathbf{B}^\mathsf{T} \widetilde{\mathbf{R}}_i - \mathbf{e}_i^{\mathsf{T}} - \mathbf{e}_{\widetilde{g}_i}^\mathsf{T})^\mathsf{T}$  is bounded by  $2^{-\Omega(\lambda)}$ , which completes the proof.

**Lemma 9.**  $\mathcal{H}_2$  is identical to  $\mathcal{H}_3$ .

*Proof.* In  $\mathcal{H}_3$ ,  $\mathbf{c}_i$  is computed by

$$\mathbf{c}_{i}^{\mathsf{T}} = (\widetilde{\mathbf{s}}_{i}^{\mathsf{T}} \mathbf{A} + \widetilde{\mathbf{e}}_{i}^{\mathsf{T}} - \mathsf{dct}_{f_{i}} - \mathsf{hct}_{i}' - \mathsf{dct}_{\widetilde{g}_{i}} + \widetilde{g}_{i}(\mathbf{x})^{\mathsf{T}} \bmod \Delta)$$

$$= \begin{pmatrix} (\mathbf{s}_{i} + \mathbf{u}_{i} + \mathbf{w}_{\widetilde{g}_{i}})^{\mathsf{T}} \mathbf{A} + (\mathbf{e}_{i}^{\mathsf{T}} + \mathbf{e}_{B}^{\mathsf{T}} \widetilde{\mathbf{R}}_{i} + \mathbf{e}_{i}'^{\mathsf{T}} + \mathbf{e}_{\widetilde{g}_{i}}^{\mathsf{T}}) - (\mathbf{u}_{i}^{\mathsf{T}} \mathbf{A} + \mathbf{e}_{i}'^{\mathsf{T}} - \mathbf{r}^{\mathsf{T}} (\mathbf{B} \widetilde{\mathbf{R}}_{i})) \\ - ((\mathbf{r}^{\mathsf{T}} \mathbf{B} + \mathbf{e}_{B}^{\mathsf{T}}) \widetilde{\mathbf{R}}_{i} - f_{i}(\mathbf{r})) - (\mathbf{w}_{\widetilde{g}_{i}}^{\mathsf{T}} \mathbf{A} + \mathbf{e}_{\widetilde{g}_{i}}^{\mathsf{T}} + \widetilde{g}_{i}(\mathbf{x})^{\mathsf{T}}) + \widetilde{g}_{i}(\mathbf{x})^{\mathsf{T}} \end{pmatrix} \bmod \Delta$$

$$= (\mathbf{s}_{i}^{\mathsf{T}} \mathbf{A} + \mathbf{e}_{i}^{\mathsf{T}} + f_{i}(\mathbf{r})^{\mathsf{T}} \bmod \Delta) = (\mathbf{s}_{i}^{\mathsf{T}} \mathbf{A} + \mathbf{e}_{i}^{\mathsf{T}} \bmod \Delta),$$

{49}------------------------------------------------

which is identical to  $\mathcal{H}_2$ . Notice that the last equation follows from the observation that  $\Delta | f_i(\mathbf{r})$ .

We note that one can similarly obtain the relation through the correctness equation (14) described in theorem 5. Assuming the required conditions for theorem 5 holds, by reordering the variables in the correctness equation (14) we get

$$\mathbf{c}_{i}^{\mathsf{T}} = \rho_{i}\mathbf{A} + \tilde{\mathbf{e}}_{i}^{\mathsf{T}} - \widetilde{g}(\mathbf{x})^{\mathsf{T}} - \underline{\mathsf{hct}}_{i}' - \mathsf{dct}_{i} - \mathsf{dct}_{i} - \mathsf{dct}_{\widetilde{g}} - \Delta \left[ \frac{\mathbf{c}_{\mathbf{s},i}^{\mathsf{T}}\mathbf{G}^{-1}(\mathbf{A}) - \mathbf{c}_{i}^{\mathsf{T}}}{\Delta} \right].$$

By taking module  $\Delta$  on both sides, this immediately gives

$$\mathbf{c}_{i}^{\mathsf{T}} = (\widetilde{\mathbf{s}}_{i}^{\mathsf{T}} \mathbf{A} + \widetilde{\mathbf{e}}_{i}^{\mathsf{T}} - \mathsf{dct}_{f_{i}} - \underline{\mathsf{hct}}_{i}' - \mathsf{dct}_{\widetilde{g}_{i}} + \widetilde{g}_{i}(\mathbf{x})^{\mathsf{T}} \bmod \Delta)$$

**Lemma 10.**  $\mathcal{H}_3$  is identical to  $\mathcal{H}_4$ .

*Proof.* This follows from the simple observation that, for every distribution  $\mathcal{D}$  and every deterministic function h,

$$\{x \leftarrow \mathcal{D}\} \equiv \left\{ x \leftarrow \mathcal{D}|_{h(x)=y} \, \middle| \, \begin{array}{l} x_0 \leftarrow \mathcal{D} \\ y = h(x_0) \end{array} \right\}. \tag{16}$$

Therefore the distribution of  $\mathbf{R}_{i}^{*}$  is identical in both hybrids. The remaining difference between the two hybrids is just a change of variables.

**Lemma 11.** If  $q < 2^n$  and  $\sigma_0 = 2^{\lambda} m^{\Omega(\log n)}$ , the statistical distance between  $\mathcal{H}_4$  and  $\mathcal{H}_5$  is bounded by  $2^{-\Omega(\lambda)}$ .

*Proof.* The only difference between the two hybrids is that in the computation of the rerandomized ciphertext  $hct'_i$ ,

$$\mathcal{H}_4$$
:  $hct'_i = \overline{\mathbf{B}}(\mathbf{R}_{0,i} - \mathbf{R}_{f_i}) \boxminus f_i(\mathbf{r}), \quad \mathcal{H}_5$ :  $hct'_i = \overline{\mathbf{B}}\mathbf{R}_{0,i} \boxminus f_i(\mathbf{r}),$ 

where  $\|\mathbf{R}_{f_i}\| \le m^{O(\log n)}$  since  $f_i$  is computable in depth  $O(\log(n\log q)) = O(\log n)$ . Therefore, by the smudging lemma (lemma 3), the distribution of  $\mathbf{R}_{0,i} \leftarrow \mathcal{D}_{\sigma_0}^{m \times \ell}$  is  $2^{-\Omega(\lambda)}$ -close to  $\mathbf{R}_{0,i} \leftarrow \mathcal{D}_{\sigma_0}^{m \times \ell} + \mathbf{R}_{f_i}$ , which completes the proof.

<span id="page-49-0"></span>**Lemma 12.** If  $\Delta \geq 2^{\lambda} \cdot \sigma \sigma_0$ , the statistical distance between  $\mathcal{H}_5$  and  $\mathcal{H}_6$  is bounded by  $2^{-\Omega(\lambda)}$ .

*Proof.* In  $\mathcal{H}_6$ , the output of  $\widetilde{f_i}$  is

$$\begin{split} &\widetilde{f_i}(\mathsf{hct},\mathsf{hct}_{0,i},\mathbf{A},\mathbf{D}_i,\mathsf{dct},\widehat{\mathbf{c}}_i)^\mathsf{T} \\ &= \Delta \left[ \frac{\widehat{\mathbf{c}}_i^\mathsf{T}\mathbf{G}^{-1}(\mathbf{A}) + \mathsf{vec}(\mathbf{G}^{-1}(-\overline{\mathsf{hct}}_{0,i}))^\mathsf{T} \cdot \mathsf{dct} + \underline{\mathsf{hct}}_{0,i}}{\Delta} \right] \\ &= \Delta \left[ \frac{(\mathbf{r}^\mathsf{T}\mathbf{D}\mathbf{G}^{-1}(\mathbf{A}) + \mathbf{e}_{\mathbf{s},i}^\mathsf{T}\mathbf{G}^{-1}(\mathbf{A}) - \mathbf{u}_i^\mathsf{T}\mathbf{A}) + (\mathbf{u}_i^\mathsf{T}\mathbf{A} + \mathbf{e}_i'^\mathsf{T} - \mathbf{r}^\mathsf{T}(\mathbf{B}\mathbf{R}_{0,i})) + (\mathbf{r}^\mathsf{T}\mathbf{B}\mathbf{R}_{0,i} + \mathbf{e}_\mathbf{B}^\mathsf{T}\mathbf{R}_{0,i})}{\Delta} \right] \\ &= \Delta \left[ \frac{\mathbf{r}^\mathsf{T}\mathbf{D}\mathbf{G}^{-1}(\mathbf{A}) + \mathbf{e}_{\mathbf{s},i}^\mathsf{T} + \mathbf{e}_i'^\mathsf{T} + \mathbf{e}_\mathbf{B}^\mathsf{T}\mathbf{R}_{0,i}}{\Delta} \right]. \end{split}$$

{50}------------------------------------------------

Notice that the term  $\mathbf{r}^{\mathsf{T}}\mathbf{D}\mathbf{G}^{-1}(\mathbf{A})$  is marginally random given that  $\mathbf{r}$ ,  $\mathbf{A}$ ,  $\mathbf{D}$  are all sampled uniform randomly, and that with probability  $2^{-\Omega(\lambda)}$ , the error vector has norm bounded by

$$\left\|\mathbf{e}_{\mathbf{s},i}^{\mathsf{T}} + \mathbf{e}_{i}^{\mathsf{T}} + \mathbf{e}_{\mathbf{B}}^{\mathsf{T}} \mathbf{R}_{0,i}\right\| \leq \sigma \sqrt{\lambda} + \sigma \sqrt{\lambda} \cdot \ell n + \sigma \sqrt{\lambda} \cdot m \cdot \sigma_{0} \sqrt{\lambda} \leq \mathsf{poly}(\lambda) \cdot \sigma \sigma_{0}.$$

Therefore by lemma 4, we have

$$\widetilde{f_i}(\mathsf{hct},\mathsf{hct}_{0,i},\mathbf{A},\mathbf{D}_i,\mathsf{dct},\widehat{\mathbf{c}}_i)^{\mathsf{T}} = \Delta \left\lfloor \frac{\mathbf{r}^{\mathsf{T}}\mathbf{D}\mathbf{G}^{-1}(\mathbf{A}) + \mathbf{e}_{\mathbf{s},i}^{\mathsf{T}} + \mathbf{e}_i^{\mathsf{T}} + \mathbf{e}_B^{\mathsf{T}}\mathbf{R}_{0,i}}{\Delta} \right\rfloor = \Delta \left\lfloor \frac{\mathbf{r}^{\mathsf{T}}\mathbf{D}\mathbf{G}^{-1}(\mathbf{A})}{\Delta} \right\rfloor = f_i(\mathbf{r})^{\mathsf{T}}$$

with probability at least  $(\text{poly}(\lambda) \cdot \sigma \sigma_0)/\Delta + 2^{-\Omega(\lambda)} = 2^{-\Omega(\lambda)}$ , which completes the proof.

As a remark, the relation between  $f_i$  and  $\tilde{f_i}$  arises from the correctness equation (14), following similar arguments given in claim 1 in section 4.

<span id="page-50-0"></span>**Lemma 13.** If  $\Delta = 2^{\Omega(\lambda)} \cdot \sigma \sigma_0$ , then  $\mathcal{H}_6$  and  $\mathcal{H}_7$  are  $\epsilon$ -computationally indistinguishable for all polynomial sized adversaries assuming  $\epsilon(\lambda)$  security for the CRO assumption with parameters  $(n, q, \Delta, \sigma)$  (assumption 1).

*Proof.* Let  $(f^{\text{circ}}, f^{\text{CRO}}, \widetilde{f}^{\text{CRO}})$  be the function tuple defined in assumption 1 with respect to LWE parameters  $(n, q, \Delta, \sigma)$ , for polynomial parameters  $(Q, \ell)$  of the functional encoding. We start by arguing that one can perfectly simulate the distribution  $\mathcal{H}_6$  with the real distribution  $\mathcal{D}_0$  of the  $(f^{\text{circ}}, f_{\text{CRO}}, \widetilde{f}_{\text{CRO}})$ -CRO assumption. For (hpk, hct, hct<sub>0</sub>,  $\mathbf{A}$ ,  $\mathbf{D}$ , ct<sub>1</sub>, ct<sub>2</sub>,  $\mathbf{R}^*$ )  $\leftarrow \mathcal{D}_0$ , observe that

- hpk =  $\overline{\mathbf{B}}$ , hct =  $\overline{\mathbf{B}}\mathbf{R}$  + bits( $\mathbf{r}$ )<sup>T</sup>  $\otimes$   $\mathbf{G}$ , hct<sub>0</sub> =  $\overline{\mathbf{B}}\mathbf{R}$ <sub>0</sub> are computed identically as  $\mathcal{H}_6$
- **A**, **D** are sampled at random, identical to  $\mathcal{H}_6$ .
- $ct_1 = \mathbf{U}^\mathsf{T} \mathbf{A} + \mathbf{E}_{\mathbf{A}} + \mathbf{I}_{\ell} \otimes \mathbf{G}_n^\mathsf{T} \mathbf{r}$ , identical to the component dct in  $\mathcal{H}_6$
- $\operatorname{ct}_{2,i} = \mathbf{r}^{\mathsf{T}} \mathbf{D}_i + \mathbf{e}_{\mathbf{D},i}^{\mathsf{T}} + f_i^{\operatorname{circ}}(\mathbf{U}, \operatorname{hct}_0) = \mathbf{r}^{\mathsf{T}} \mathbf{D}_i + \mathbf{e}_{\mathbf{D},i}^{\mathsf{T}} \operatorname{vec}(\mathbf{G}^{-1}(-\overline{\operatorname{hct}}_{0,i})) \cdot \mathbf{U}^{\mathsf{T}} \mathbf{G}$ , which is identical to the computation of  $\widehat{\mathbf{c}}_i$  in  $\mathcal{H}_6$  since  $\overline{\operatorname{hct}}_i' = \overline{\operatorname{hct}}_{0,i}$ .
- The opening  $\mathbf{R}^*$  is sampled from discrete Gaussian conditioning on  $\mathbf{B}\mathbf{R}_i^* = \mathsf{hct}_{f_i} \boxplus \mathsf{hct}_{0,i} \boxminus \widetilde{f}_i^{\mathsf{CRO}}(\mathsf{enc})$ . Note that the function  $\widetilde{f}^{\mathsf{CRO}}$  is of the form

$$\widetilde{f}_i^{\mathsf{CRO}}(\mathsf{hct},\mathsf{hct}_0,\mathbf{A},\mathbf{D},\mathsf{ct}_1,\mathsf{ct}_2)^{\mathsf{T}} = \Delta \left[ \frac{\mathsf{ct}_{2,i} \cdot \mathbf{G}^{-1}(\mathbf{A}) + \mathsf{vec}(\mathbf{G}^{-1}(-\overline{\mathsf{hct}}_{0,i}))^{\mathsf{T}}\mathsf{ct}_1 + \underline{\mathsf{hct}}_{0,i}}{\Delta} \right],$$

which is identical to the function  $f_i$  defined in  $\mathcal{H}_6$  after establishing the equality  $\mathsf{ct}_1 = \mathsf{dct}$  and  $\mathsf{ct}_{2,i} = \widehat{\mathsf{c}}_i$ . Therefore  $\mathbf{R}^*$  sampled from the CRO real distribution distributes identically with  $\mathbf{R}^*$  sampled  $\mathcal{H}_6$ 

Furthermore, the remaining elements in  $\mathcal{H}_6$ , including  $\mathbf{c}_i$ ,  $\mathsf{dct}_x$ , and  $\tilde{\mathbf{s}}$ , can be computed/sampled given the samples listed in the above comparison. This directly gives a simulator of  $\mathcal{H}_6$  given  $\mathcal{D}_0$  from CRO.

Now, following the CRO assumption the samples given by the real distribution  $\mathcal{D}_0$  is indistinguishable from the ideal distribution  $\mathcal{D}_1$ , where (hpk, hct, hct<sub>0</sub>,  $\mathbf{A}$ ,  $\mathbf{D}$ , ct<sub>1</sub> = dct, ct<sub>2</sub> =  $\{\hat{\mathbf{c}}_i\}_{i\in[Q]}$ ) are all sampled at random, and  $\mathbf{R}^*$  is sampled with respect to the random elements. This is exactly the output distribution of  $\mathcal{H}_7$ . Therefore,  $\mathcal{H}_6$  and  $\mathcal{H}_7$  are  $\epsilon(\lambda)$ -computationally indistinguishable assuming  $\epsilon$  security for the CRO assumption.

{51}------------------------------------------------

**Lemma 14.** If  $m \ge 3n \log q$ , the statistical distance between  $\mathcal{H}_7$  and  $\mathcal{H}_8$  is bounded by  $2^{-\Omega(\lambda)}$ .

*Proof.* This follows directly from the statistical randomness property of lattice trapdoors (lemma 5).

**Lemma 15.** If  $m \ge 3n \log q$  and  $\sigma_0 > m \log n$ , the statistical distance between  $\mathcal{H}_8$  and  $\mathcal{H}_9$  is bounded by  $2^{-\Omega(\lambda)}$ .

*Proof.* This follows directly from the preimage sampling property of lattice trapdoors (lemma 5).

**Lemma 16.**  $\mathcal{H}_9$  is identical to  $\mathcal{H}_{10}$ .

*Proof.* It is easy to observe that the distribution of  $\hat{c}_i$  is uniformly random in both hybrids.

**Lemma 17.** If  $\Delta = 2^{\lambda} \cdot \ell^{\Omega(d)} \sigma$ , the statistical distance between  $\mathcal{H}_{10}$  and  $\mathcal{H}_{11}$  is bounded by  $2^{-\Omega(\lambda)}$ .

*Proof.* In  $\mathcal{H}_{11}$ , the output of  $\tilde{f}'$  is

$$\begin{split} &\widetilde{f}_i'(\mathsf{hct},\mathsf{hct}_{0,i},\mathbf{A},\mathbf{D}_i,\mathsf{dct},\mathsf{dct}_{\mathbf{x}},\mathbf{c}_{\mathbf{s},i},\widetilde{\mathbf{s}}_i,\widetilde{g}_i(\mathbf{x}))^\mathsf{T} \\ = & \Delta \left[ \frac{\mathbf{c}_{\mathbf{s},i}^\mathsf{T}\mathbf{G}^{-1}(\mathbf{A}) - \widetilde{\mathbf{s}}_i^\mathsf{T}\mathbf{A} + \mathsf{dct}_{\widetilde{g}_i} - \widetilde{g}_i(\mathbf{x})^\mathsf{T} + \mathsf{vec}(\mathbf{G}^{-1}(-\overline{\mathsf{hct}}_{0,i}))^\mathsf{T} \cdot \mathsf{dct} + \underline{\mathsf{hct}}_{0,i}}{\Delta} \right] \\ = & \Delta \left[ \frac{(\widetilde{\mathbf{c}}_i^\mathsf{T}\mathbf{G}^{-1}(\mathbf{A}) + \widetilde{\mathbf{s}}_i^\mathsf{T}\mathbf{A} - \mathbf{w}_{\widetilde{g}_i}^\mathsf{T}\mathbf{A}) - \widetilde{\mathbf{s}}_i^\mathsf{T}\mathbf{A} + (\mathbf{w}_{\widetilde{g}_i}^\mathsf{T}\mathbf{A} + \mathbf{e}_{\widetilde{g}_i}^\mathsf{T} + \widetilde{g}_i(\mathbf{x}))^\mathsf{T} - \widetilde{g}_i(\mathbf{x})^\mathsf{T} + \mathsf{vec}(\mathbf{G}^{-1}(-\overline{\mathsf{hct}}_{0,i})) \cdot \mathsf{dct} + \underline{\mathsf{hct}}_{0,i}}{\Delta} \right] \\ = & \Delta \left[ \frac{(\widetilde{\mathbf{c}}_i^\mathsf{T}\mathbf{G}^{-1}(\mathbf{A}) + \mathsf{vec}(\mathbf{G}^{-1}(-\overline{\mathsf{hct}}_{0,i})))^\mathsf{T} \cdot \mathsf{dct} + \underline{\mathsf{hct}}_{0,i}}{\Delta} \right], \end{split}$$

where the major terms  $\mathbf{t}^{\mathsf{T}} = (\widehat{\mathbf{c}}_i^{\mathsf{T}} \mathbf{G}^{-1}(\mathbf{A}) + \text{vec}(\mathbf{G}^{-1}(-\overline{\mathsf{hct}}_{0,i}))^{\mathsf{T}} \cdot \det + \underline{\mathsf{hct}}_{0,i})$  has uniformly random marginal distribution given that  $\underline{\mathsf{hct}}_{0,i}$  is random and independent to the remaining terms, and the error term has norm bounded by  $\|\mathbf{e}_{\widetilde{g}_i}\| \leq \ell^{O(d)} \sigma \sqrt{\lambda}$  with  $1 - 2^{-\Omega(\lambda)}$  probability. Therefore, again by lemma 4, we have with probability  $1 - 2^{-\Omega(\lambda)}$ ,

$$\widetilde{f}'_{i}(\mathsf{hct},\mathsf{hct}_{0,i},\mathbf{A},\mathbf{D}_{i},\mathsf{dct},\mathsf{dct}_{x},\mathbf{c}_{\mathbf{s},i},\widetilde{\mathbf{s}}_{i},\widetilde{g}_{i}(\mathbf{x}))^{\mathsf{T}} = \Delta \left\lfloor \frac{\mathbf{t}^{\mathsf{T}} + \mathbf{e}_{\widetilde{g}_{i}}^{\mathsf{T}}}{\Delta} \right\rfloor = \Delta \left\lfloor \frac{\mathbf{t}^{\mathsf{T}}}{\Delta} \right\rfloor = \widetilde{f}_{i}(\mathsf{hct},\mathsf{hct}_{0,i},\mathbf{A},\mathbf{D}_{i},\mathsf{dct},\widehat{\mathbf{c}}_{i})^{\mathsf{T}},$$

which completes the proof.

<span id="page-51-0"></span>**Lemma 18.** Assuming  $\epsilon(\lambda)$  security for LWE<sub>n,q,\sigma</sub> (Assumption 1), then  $\mathcal{H}_{11}$  and  $\mathcal{H}_{12}$  are  $\epsilon(\lambda)$ -computationally indistinguishable for all polynomial sized adversaries.

*Proof.* Assuming  $\epsilon(\lambda)$  security for LWE<sub> $n,q,\sigma$ </sub> we immediately have that the following two ensembles are  $\epsilon(\lambda)$ -computationally indistinguishable

$$\begin{cases}
\operatorname{dct}_{\mathbf{x}} = \mathbf{W}^{\mathsf{T}} \mathbf{A} + \mathbf{E}_{\mathbf{x}} + \mathbf{x} \otimes \mathbf{G}^{\mathsf{T}} \middle| & \mathbf{A} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_{q}^{n \times K\ell \lceil \log q \rceil} \\
\mathbf{W} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_{q}^{n \times K\ell \lceil \log q \rceil \times \ell}
\end{cases} \approx_{c}^{\epsilon} \left\{ \operatorname{dct}_{\mathbf{x}} = \mathbf{V} + \mathbf{x} \otimes \mathbf{G}^{\mathsf{T}} \middle| \mathbf{V} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_{q}^{K\ell \lceil \log q \rceil \times \ell} \right\}.$$

{52}------------------------------------------------

The right distribution is identical to sampling  $\mathsf{dct}_x$  at random, matching the sampling procedure in  $\mathcal{H}_{12}$ . Therefore,  $\mathcal{H}_{11}$  and  $\mathcal{H}_{12}$  is also  $\epsilon(\lambda)$ -indistinguishable.

Assuming (subexponential) security for CRO  $^9$ ,  $n = \text{poly}(\lambda)$ ,  $q < 2^n$ ,  $m = \Omega(n \log q)$ ,  $\sigma_e \ge 2^{\lambda} \sigma \sigma_0 \ell^{\Omega(\log n + d)}$ ,  $\sigma_0 \ge 2^{\lambda} m^{\Omega(\log n)} \sigma$ , and  $\Delta \ge 2^{\lambda} \ell^{\Omega(d)} \sigma \sigma_0$ , where m,  $\sigma_0$ ,  $\sigma_e$ ,  $\Delta$  are sufficiently large, then all conditions required by the above lemmas are satisfied. Therefore, combining lemmas 7 to 18, we immediately know that  $\mathcal{H}_0$  and  $\mathcal{H}_{12}$  are sub-exponentially indistinguishable, which completes the proof.

**Parameter instantiation** We now give a set of plausible parameters toward a sub-exponentially secure functional encoding scheme. In the following, we use the notation  $\widetilde{O}(\cdot)$  for the asymptotic notation suppressing all terms of order poly  $\log(\lambda, k, L, d)$ .

Let  $\delta \in (0,1)$  be the LWE modulus-to-noise ratio parameter. We set our variables as follow.

- $\kappa = L^{0.1\delta}$ ,  $\ell = L^{1-0.1\delta}$ ,
- $n = \widetilde{O}(\lambda L^{0.1\delta} d)^{1/\delta}$ ,  $m = O(n \cdot \text{poly log } n)$ ,
- $\sigma = poly(\lambda)$ ,
- $\sigma_0 = 2^{\lambda} m^{O(\log n)} \sigma = 2^{O(\lambda)} n^{O(\log n)}$
- $\sigma_{\mathbf{e}} = 2^{\lambda} \sigma \sigma_0 \ell^{O(d + \log n)} \leq 2^{O(\lambda)} L^{O(d + \log n)}$
- $\Delta = 2^{\lambda} \ell^{O(d)} \sigma \sigma_0 \leq 2^{O(\lambda)} L^{O(d + \log n)}$
- $p = O(\lambda(\ell + m)^{O(d + \log n)} \sigma \sigma_{\mathbf{e}} + \Delta) \le 2^{O(\lambda)} (n + L)^{O(d + \log n)}$  where  $\Delta | p$ .
- $q = 2^{\kappa}p = 2^{O(\lambda)}(n+L)^{O(d+\log n)} \cdot 2^{L^{0.1\delta}}$ , where  $\log q = O(\lambda) + (d+\log n)\log(n+L)L^{0.1\delta} = \widetilde{O}(\lambda L^{0.1\delta}d) \le n^{\delta}$ .

Under the parameter setting, construction construction 1 is correct, succinct, and subexponentially SIM-secure. Therefore, we immediately get the following theorem.

**Theorem 8.** Assuming the subexponential CRO assumption (assumption 1), there exists a subexponentially secure functional encoding scheme for all polynomial-sized circuits.

# <span id="page-52-0"></span>6 Oblivious LWE Sampling from IND-CRO Assumption

In this section, we formulate a weaker indistinguishability version of the CRO assumption (IND-CRO), and show that IND-CRO assumption implies an Oblivious LWE Sampler [WW21], which also implies functional encodings.

<span id="page-52-1"></span><sup>&</sup>lt;sup>9</sup>Note that CRO readily implies LWE with the same parameters  $(n, q, \sigma)$ .

{53}------------------------------------------------

#### <span id="page-53-0"></span>6.1 The IND-CRO Assumption

The IND-CRO assumption shares the same structure as the CRO assumption, but instead of stating the pseudorandomness of the ciphertexts and LWE samples, the IND-CRO assumption states that the samples jointly hide a secret bit  $\beta$ . The left and right distributions  $\mathcal{D}_{\beta}$  of IND-CRO both augment the real distributions in CRO with an additional LWE sample  $\mathsf{ct}_0$  w.r.t. public matrix  $\mathbf{A}$  that uses independent secrets  $\mathbf{W}$ , and hides the secret bit  $\beta$  in the form  $\beta \mathbf{G}_{\ell}^{\mathsf{T}}$ . Additionally, the LWE sample  $\mathsf{ct}_2$  that used to hide just a circular function  $f^{\mathsf{circ}}(\mathbf{U},\mathsf{hct}_0)$  of the secret  $\mathbf{U}$  and  $\mathsf{hct}_0$ , also hides (the concatenation of) linear functions of  $\mathbf{W}$  of form  $-\mathbf{G}_{\ell}^{-1}(\mathbf{v}_i)^{\mathsf{T}}\mathbf{W}^{\mathsf{T}}\mathbf{G}_n$  and functions of  $\beta$  of form  $-\beta \hat{\mathbf{s}}_i^{\mathsf{T}}\mathbf{G}_n$ , where  $\mathbf{v}_i^{\mathsf{T}} = \hat{\mathbf{s}}_i^{\mathsf{T}}\mathbf{A} + \widehat{\mathbf{e}}_i^{\mathsf{T}}$  are fresh LWE samples w.r.t. public matrix  $\mathbf{A}$ .

We now formally define the  $(f^{circ}, f, \widetilde{f})$ -IND-CRO assumptions.

<span id="page-53-2"></span>**Definition 11** (( $f^{\text{circ}}$ , f,  $\widetilde{f}$ )-Indistinguishability Circular Security with Random Opening (CRO) Assumption). Let  $\lambda$  be the security parameter. Let n, m, d, k',  $\ell$ , M,  $\sigma$  be integer parameters that are polynomial in  $\lambda$ , and q,  $\sigma_0$  be (potentially superpolynomial) integer parameters where  $m = \Omega(n \log q)$  and  $\sigma_0 = 2^{\lambda} m^{\Omega(d)}$  are sufficiently large. Let  $f \in \mathcal{F}_{d,M}$  be a bounded depth packed circuit (definition 5) which parses its input as bits and have depth bound d and output length M, where M w.l.o.g. is a multiple of  $(n+1)\lceil \log q \rceil$  and  $f^{\text{circ}}$  and  $\widetilde{f}$  be efficiently computable functions with domain/codomain implicitly defined in Figure 9.

We say that the (subexponential) ( $f^{circ}$ , f,  $\tilde{f}$ )-CRO assumption holds if  $\mathcal{D}_0$  and  $\mathcal{D}_1$  in Figure 9 are (sub-exponentially) indistinguishable to all polynomial time attackers.

$$\begin{split} &\left\{\left(\mathsf{hpk},\mathsf{enc}=\left(\mathsf{hct},\mathsf{hct}_{0},\mathbf{A},\mathbf{D},\{\mathbf{v}_{i}\}_{i\in[k']},\mathsf{ct}_{0},\mathsf{ct}_{1},\mathsf{ct}_{2}\right)\right)\,\middle|\,\left(\mathsf{hpk},\mathsf{enc},\mathsf{hint}\right)\leftarrow\mathcal{D}_{0}(\mathbf{v})\right\}_{\lambda}\\ &\approx\left\{\left(\mathsf{hpk},\mathsf{enc}=\left(\mathsf{hct},\mathsf{hct}_{0},\mathbf{A},\mathbf{D},\{\mathbf{v}_{i}\}_{i\in[k']},\mathsf{ct}_{0},\mathsf{ct}_{1},\mathsf{ct}_{2}\right)\right)\,\middle|\,\left(\mathsf{hpk},\mathsf{enc},\mathsf{hint}\right)\leftarrow\mathcal{D}_{1}(\mathbf{v})\right\}_{\lambda} \end{split}$$

Similar to the case of the CRO assumption, to construct the oblivious LWE sampler, it suffices to assume the IND-CRO assumption for specific tuples of functions. By default, the IND-CRO assumption refers to this version.

<span id="page-53-1"></span>**Assumption 3** (Indistinguishability Circular Security with Random Opening (IND-CRO) Assumption). Let  $\lambda$  be the security parameter, and n, q,  $\sigma$  be LWE parameters dependent on  $\lambda$ , where  $\sigma = \text{poly}(\lambda)$ ,  $q \leq 2^{n^{\delta}}$  for some constant  $\delta \in (0,1)$ , q is a multiple of  $\Delta$  such that  $q/\Delta \geq 2^{\lambda}$ , and  $\Delta \geq (2n \log q)^{\lambda}$ . The (subexponential) IND-CRO assumption with parameters  $(n,q,\sigma,\Delta)$  states that for an appropriate  $m = \Theta(n \log q)$ ,  $\sigma_0 = \Delta/2^{\Theta(\lambda)}$ , and every efficiently computable polynomials  $Q = Q(\lambda)$  and  $\ell = \ell(\lambda)$ , the (subexponential)  $(f^{\text{circ}}, f, \widetilde{f})$ -IND-CRO assumption holds for the following function tuple, where  $(f^{\text{circ}}, f)$  are identical to assumption 1:

$$\begin{split} & \mathsf{hct}_0 = \begin{pmatrix} \overline{\mathsf{hct}}_{0,i} \in \mathbb{Z}_q^{n \times \ell} \\ \underline{\mathsf{hct}}_{0,i} \in \mathbb{Z}_q^{1 \times \ell} \end{pmatrix}_{i \in [Q]} \quad \mathbf{D} = \left( \mathbf{D}_i \in \mathbb{Z}_q^{n \times n \lceil \log q \rceil} \right)_{i \in [Q]} \\ & \mathsf{ct}_2 = \left( \mathsf{ct}_{2,i} = \mathbf{r}^\mathsf{T} \mathbf{D}_i + \mathbf{e}_{\mathbf{D},i} + f_i^{\mathsf{circ}}(\mathbf{U}, \mathsf{hct}_{0,i}) - \mathbf{G}_\ell^{-1}(\mathbf{v}_i)^\mathsf{T} \mathbf{W}^\mathsf{T} \mathbf{G}_n - \beta \hat{\mathbf{s}}_i^\mathsf{T} \mathbf{G}_n \right)_{i \in [Q]}, \text{ where } \mathbf{e}_{\mathbf{D}} = \{\mathbf{e}_{\mathbf{D},i}\}_{i \in [Q]} \\ & f^{\mathsf{circ}} = \left( f_i^{\mathsf{circ}} \right)_{i \in [Q]} \qquad f = \left( f_i \right)_{i \in [Q]} \qquad \widetilde{f} = \left( \widetilde{f}_i \right)_{i \in [Q]} \\ & f^{\mathsf{circ}}_i(\mathbf{U}, \mathsf{hct}_0) = -\mathsf{vec}(\mathbf{G}_n^{-1}(-\overline{\mathsf{hct}}_{0,i}))^\mathsf{T} \cdot (\mathbf{U}^\mathsf{T} \mathbf{G}_n) \\ & f_i(\mathbf{r}, \mathbf{A}, \mathbf{D})^\mathsf{T} = \Delta \left[ \frac{\mathbf{r}^\mathsf{T} \mathbf{D}_i \cdot \mathbf{G}_n^{-1}(\mathbf{A})}{\Delta} \right] \\ & \widetilde{f}_i(\mathsf{hct}, \mathsf{hct}_0, \mathbf{A}, \mathbf{D}, \{\mathbf{v}_i\}_{i \in Q}, \mathsf{ct}_0, \mathsf{ct}_1, \mathsf{ct}_2)^\mathsf{T} = \Delta \left[ \frac{\mathsf{ct}_{2,i} \cdot \mathbf{G}_n^{-1}(\mathbf{A}) + \mathsf{vec}(\mathbf{G}_n^{-1}(-\overline{\mathsf{hct}}_{0,i}))^\mathsf{T} \mathsf{ct}_1 + \mathbf{G}_\ell^{-1}(\mathbf{v}_i)^\mathsf{T} \mathsf{ct}_0 + \underline{\mathsf{hct}}_{0,i}}{\Delta} \right] \end{split}$$

{54}------------------------------------------------

$$\mathsf{ct}_2 = \mathbf{r}^\mathsf{T} \mathbf{D} + \mathbf{e}_{\mathbf{D}}^\mathsf{T} + f^{\mathsf{circ}}(\mathbf{U}, \mathsf{hct}_0)$$
